1935.06.23

Qin Dechun Arrives in Beiping; Negotiations on the Chahar Incident to Begin Immediately; Meeting with Doihara and Others Scheduled for Today; Xiao Zhenying Returns to Beiping from Hankou; Ambassador Chiang Visits Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota 1

(Beiping) Acting Chairman of the Chahar Provincial Government, Qin Dechun, accompanied by Security Commander Zhang Yunrong, arrived in Beiping this morning from Zhangjiakou, and it is scheduled to begin consultations with Matsui and others on the Chahar Province incident today. This morning, Qin met with He Qigong, Hou Cheng, and others at his residence. At 11:00 AM, he visited Bao Wen-yue at the Military Affairs Committee to discuss the recent situation in Chahar Province. (22nd Dispatch)

(Beiping) Qin Dechun stated, "I went to Zhangjiakou a few days ago to take up my post at the Provincial Government. Now that Matsui and others have come to Beiping, it has been decided that the consultations on the Chahar incident will take place in Beiping. I have just arrived in Beiping from Zhangjiakou. After meeting with various parties today, negotiations can begin tomorrow. This matter can be resolved peacefully. The Chahar Province area is peaceful, and the Chahar Province army, in addition to maintaining order, is committed to resolving matters peacefully." (22nd Dispatch)

(Beiping) Matsui stated, "It has been decided that negotiations on the Chahar Province incident will take place in Beiping. Qin Dechun arrived in Beiping this morning, and I plan to visit him this afternoon to discuss everything. Doihara will not participate in these negotiations; I will handle the negotiations with Qin alone." (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Qin Dechun's arrival in Beiping indicates that the Chahar incident will still be resolved in Beiping within the scope of a local matter. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Matsui is scheduled to meet with Qin Dechun on the evening of the 22nd to exchange views. After Wang Kemin arrives in Beiping on the 23rd, Doihara will present matters for discussion and decision. (22nd Dispatch)

(Beiping) Qin Dechun stated that he did not meet with the Japanese on the 22nd, and is scheduled to meet with Doihara and Matsui on the 23rd. The negotiations on the Zhangbei incident are generally showing signs of progress, and it is hoped that no further difficulties will arise in the future. (22nd Dispatch)

(Beiping) Xiao Zhenying went to Chengdu a few days ago to meet with Chiang Kai-shek and report on the recent military and political situation in Chahar Province. He arrived in Beiping tonight after completing his mission. (22nd Dispatch)

(Beiping) Qin Dechun arrived in Beiping at 8:00 AM on the 22nd with Zhang Chongrong. After getting off the train, they immediately returned to their residence. Then, accompanied by Hou Cheng, they went to Jurentang to visit Bao Wen-yue. It was decided that they would meet with Matsui, the military liaison officer of the Japanese army stationed in Zhangjiakou, in the afternoon to discuss the Zhangbei incident. According to Matsui's words to reporters, he is scheduled to meet with Director Qin in the afternoon or evening to have preliminary discussions on the Zhangbei incident, which is expected to be resolved soon. The Japanese side has no specific demands. Doihara will not participate in the discussions and is in Beiping waiting to meet with Wang Kemin. He will return to Tianjin in the next few days. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) Xiao Zhenying returned to Beiping from Hankou at 9:50 PM on the 22nd. After getting off the train, he rushed to the German Hospital to see his sick wife. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) A reporter asked Qin Dechun, the acting chairman of Chahar Province, on the 22nd about the recent progress in negotiations on the Zhangbei incident. He said that the matter is currently being discussed directly and indirectly by the parties concerned, and has not yet reached a final resolution. He personally is determined to handle this matter with the utmost sincerity, but the main aspects of the process must be reported to and instructed by the central government. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) Qin Dechun arrived here from Zhangjiakou this morning to negotiate with the Japanese on the Chahar incident. It is reported that the first meeting may be held this afternoon or evening at the Japanese Embassy's military attaché office. Attendees will be Qin Dechun and Matsui. It is expected that Doihara will not participate in the initial stages of the talks. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

(Beiping) This afternoon, envoys from both China and Japan frequently traveled between the hotel where Doihara is staying and Qin Dechun's residence, preparing for negotiations. Xiao Zhenying arrived in Beiping at 7:00 PM and immediately participated in the negotiations. The negotiations, which were temporarily stalled, gradually reached a compromise as the opinions of the two sides converged. Qin Dechun plans to formally meet with Doihara tomorrow. (22nd Japan Union News Dispatch)

(Beiping) Qin Dechun met with Bao Wen-yue this morning to discuss important matters for a long time. Qin told reporters that he would meet with Lieutenant Colonel Matsui tonight or tomorrow morning, but the content of the talks could not be disclosed, and it was still unknown. (22nd Japan Union News Dispatch)

(Beiping) Lieutenant Colonel Matsui visited Qin Dechun at 3:00 PM today, stating that the Japanese military's solution to the Chahar Province incident had no other intention than to ensure peace in the Far East. Qin also expressed that he had no fundamental objections. The two men talked for more than two hours before Matsui left. (22nd Japan Union News Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Tianjin Mayor Shang Zhen is scheduled to host Tianjin-Japan reporters at 3:30 PM on the 23rd to explain the truth about maintaining public order in the city. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Zhu Shiqin, section chief of the Beiping Military Affairs Committee, met with Iwai, the head of the Japanese Special Service Agency in Shanhaiguan, and returned on the 22nd. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Tao Shangming passed through Tianjin from Tangshan on the afternoon of the 22nd to go to Beiping to meet Wang Kemin. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Chinese Ambassador Chiang Tso-pin visited Foreign Minister Hirota at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at noon on the 22nd, saying that he had received orders from his government to return to China at the end of this month or early next month. Before leaving, he wanted to consult with the Minister to establish a lasting friendly relationship between China and Japan. Foreign Minister Hirota immediately understood Chiang's words and replied that he wholeheartedly agreed with establishing friendly relations between the two countries during this opportunity of exchanging ambassadors between China and Japan. He hoped that Ambassador Chiang would continue to discuss concrete work on Sino-Japanese friendship in the dozen or so days before his return to China. Chiang left after half an hour. Now that the North China issue has come to an end, and with everyone hoping for Sino-Japanese cooperation, it is hoped that the results of Ambassador Chiang's meeting with Foreign Minister Hirota will enable the Chinese government to establish a fundamental policy towards Japan. (22nd Japan Union News Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Chinese Ambassador to Japan, Chiang Tso-pin, formally visited the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 12:15 PM today and met with Foreign Minister Hirota. After offering his introductory remarks as the newly appointed ambassador, he said that due to orders from the National Government, he would temporarily return to China at the end of June or early July to report on the recent Sino-Japanese relations to the central government. Therefore, he hoped to have a full and frank discussion with the Minister before returning to China. Foreign Minister Hirota also strongly agreed, emphasizing that China and Japan should restore the original friendly relations of the two great friendly nations in Asia. He hoped that China would re-recognize Japan, evoke past intentions, and promote the resolution of outstanding issues. They exchanged opinions on the opening of Sino-Japanese relations and had a full and frank discussion. Foreign Minister Hirota also hoped to meet and discuss again with the Ambassador before his return to China, with the ideal of establishing a lasting peace between the two countries at this time. The meeting ended at 12:50 PM. Therefore, Ambassador Chiang will meet with Foreign Minister Hirota two or three times in the coming week to exchange views on Sino-Japanese issues, so as to provide important advice to the National Government. This meeting is extremely noteworthy for the future trend of Sino-Japanese relations. (22nd Electric Communication Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Chinese Ambassador Chiang Tso-pin visited Foreign Minister Hirota this morning and said that when he returns to Nanjing at the end of June or early July, he wishes to consult with Hirota to guide Sino-Japanese relations towards a permanently friendly foundation. It is heard that Chiang will continue to visit Hirota due to today's meeting. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

Wang Kemin Arrives in Tianjin Yesterday; Scheduled to Go to Beiping Tonight 2

(Beiping) Wang Kemin arrived in Tianjin from Shanghai at around 6:00 AM this morning. Leaders of various agencies, including Shang Zhen, welcomed him at the station. Several people, including He Jiecai, came with Wang. After getting off the train, Wang returned to his private residence in the British Concession to rest and met with Shang Zhen for a discussion. He is scheduled to go to Beiping by train tomorrow evening. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) At 6:40 AM on the 22nd, Wang Kemin arrived in Tianjin on the Shanghai-Beiping train. Shang Zhen led the heads of various municipal bureaus to welcome him at the main station and boarded the train to talk with him. After Wang got off the train at the East Station, he took a car back to his private residence at No. 80, 33rd Road, British Concession. Many guests visited. In the morning, Wang visited Song Zheyuan at Song's residence on Xiangzi Road in the British Concession to convey the Central Government's views on the Chahar incident and discussed it for a long time. At noon, he attended a banquet hosted by Wang Yitang at Penglai Street in the Japanese Concession, with Zhu Shen, Duan Honggang, Zeng Yujun, Cao Rulin, and others in attendance. At 3:00 PM on the 22nd, Wang Kemin visited the Japanese Army Haiguangsi Barracks in Tianjin to meet with Japanese Army Chief of Staff Sakai Takashi and Staff Officers Omaki and Ishii as a courtesy after taking office. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Wang Kemin is scheduled to take the Beiping-Yulin express train to Beiping at 4:00 PM on the 23rd. Before leaving, he will visit the commander of the Japanese army in Tianjin, Meijiro Umezu, to discuss Sino-Japanese relations and recent events in Hebei and Chahar. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Wang Kemin stated that he came north to replace Chairman Huang to conclude the unfinished cases of the Political Readjustment Committee. Current diplomacy and Hebei-Chahar affairs have become past matters and have come to an end. There should be no problems arising from them. Therefore, in addition to ending the responsibilities of previous old cases, he has no active matters to handle. The organization of the Political Committee remains the same, and all kinds of rumors are not credible. Regarding the Japanese troops stationed at various passes along the Great Wall, he plans to negotiate with the Japanese side for their withdrawal in the near future. Song Zheyuan's departure from Chahar was entirely based on national interests and was a voluntary resignation. He has not yet received news of Doihara's visit to Beiping and will only know if there is anything to discuss when they meet. Chairman He has the intention of returning to the north in the near future. He will stay in Tianjin for one day to meet with Song Zheyuan and Shang Zhen before going to Beiping to take up his post. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) At 2:00 PM on the 22nd, Wang Kemin visited Shang Zhen at the Xihu Hotel to discuss Tianjin's local diplomacy and public security, and exchanged views for a long time. At 7:00 PM, Shang Zhen hosted a banquet at the Xihu Villa, inviting many Tianjin gentlemen to accompany him. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Wang Kemin arrived in Tianjin by train at 7:00 AM on the 22nd. Shang Zhen, Wang Yitang, Hu Zhengzhi, and Gu Rugeng boarded the train at the new station to greet him. After Wang got off the train at the old station, he went directly to his private residence. He then went out to meet with the press, stating that his coming north was at the behest of the central government to end the Hebei and Zhangbei incidents and stabilize local morale. The Political Readjustment Committee would abide by the established rules in handling everything and would not change. He Yingqin is expected to return to Beiping soon after being urged by all parties. There is no news in the capital regarding the candidates for the reorganization of the Hebei Provincial Government. Regarding the newly arrived Japanese troops in the areas of Gubeikou and Dongling, Wang said that he would negotiate with the Japanese side for their withdrawal in Beiping. Wang rested at his residence and went to the Municipal Government to visit Shang Zhen at 11:00 AM, and decided to leave Tianjin for Beiping on the evening of the 23rd. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The newly appointed Director of the Tianjin Municipal Finance Bureau, Han Haicheng, arrived at the bureau at 4:00 PM on the 22nd with the personnel for the takeover to take up his post. He stated that the city's revenue and expenditure will be absolutely transparent in the future, taken from the people and used for the people. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The acting chairman of the Beiping Political Readjustment Committee, Wang Kemin, arrived in Tianjin this morning and denied the rumors that the Beiping Political Readjustment Committee was about to be abolished. Several Chinese officials went to welcome Wang when he arrived in Tianjin. Wang is scheduled to go to Beiping tomorrow morning. He is confident that the outstanding issues between China and Japan can be completely resolved in Beiping soon. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

(Beiping) Wang Kemin is scheduled to come to Beiping tomorrow evening. (22nd Japan Union News Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Wang Kemin arrived in Tianjin this morning. At 2:00 PM, he visited Staff Officer Sakai to express his congratulations on his new post and exchanged views on the post-Sino-Japanese issues in North China. Wang is scheduled to formally meet with Commander Umezu tomorrow morning. (22nd Japan Union News Dispatch)

No Sign of Withdrawal of Japanese Troops Stationed in Gubeikou 3

(Beiping) The Kawagishi Unit of the Japanese army brigade stationed in Gubeikou is still stationed in the same place, without advancing, but there is no sign of withdrawal. The local area is as peaceful as before. When the Japanese troops arrived at Gubeikou, they stated that it was purely an exercise and that they would withdraw in one month. Therefore, the withdrawal of these Japanese troops should be around the beginning of next month. (22nd Dispatch)

(Beiping) Okabe, entrusted by the Japanese Kwantung Army, has completed his business in Beiping and is scheduled to leave Beiping for Changchun on the 23rd. (22nd Dispatch)

Ninghai to Lead the Haiqi and Haishen Ships Back North; Cantonese Faction Sends Gan Jiai-hou to Hong Kong for Investigation; Jiang Xiyuan and Others Remain in Imprisonment 4

(Hong Kong) The Central Government sent three ships south this time, including the Ninghai, Hairong, and Haichou, led by Chen Jiliang. The Ninghai sailed into Hong Kong harbor, and the rest anchored off Chai Wan outside Hong Kong. It is heard that the Yingrui and Yixian are also rushing here. Chen landed at 8:00 AM on the 22nd to visit the Governor of Hong Kong. At noon, the Governor of Hong Kong returned the visit to the Ninghai. (22nd Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Cao Yujian, navigator of the Haiqi, said on the 22nd that the Haiqi and Haishen passed Hengtang at 6:45 PM on the 21st and encountered the Ninghai, Hairong, and Haichou sailing in a character shape. The Ninghai was in the lead, raising the commander's flag and firing more than 30 cannons. (22nd Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Ninghai arrived in Hong Kong late at night on the 21st and anchored in Kowloon Bay at 2:00 AM on the 22nd. At 8:00 AM, Xue Yu, the commander of the Hong Kong Navy, sent his chief of staff to visit Chen Jiliang, the commander of the Haiqi. At 9:00 AM, the two sides exchanged gun salutes to pay their respects. Acting Governor of Hong Kong, Shaw Dun, also visited the ship at 12:30 PM. It is heard that the Ninghai will add coal and water and lead the Haiqi and Haishen north. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Haiqi, Haishen, and Zhaohe ships of the navy stationed in Guangdong suddenly left Guangdong on the 15th due to a dispute over funding. The Zhaohe temporarily did not leave due to engine damage. The details have been reported in the newspapers in recent days. After receiving reports from Chen Jitang and the escaped ships, the Central Government sent warships currently conducting naval exercises to monitor them to avoid accidents. However, those with ulterior motives fabricated rumors, intending to provoke, falsely claiming that the Central Government had instigated the situation beforehand and had threatened to blockade Guangzhou. It is not known that warships belong to the country and cannot be divided by their location. A reporter from the Central News Agency asked a senior naval official about the cause of this incident. According to him, the navy should be unified and obey the Central Government and the Navy Department. This is the case in all countries with navies. Due to various complex circumstances, China's navy has failed to follow normal procedures, resulting in an abnormal situation. It is heard that the Haiqi and Haishen will return to the naval establishment to realize naval unification. Warships currently conducting naval exercises have been dispatched to handle the matter. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Guangzhou) The local authorities here are paying close attention to the news of the new developments outside Hong Kong last night. It is heard that Gan Jiai-hou has been sent to Hong Kong to closely monitor the situation. It is likely that the authorities will not decide on any action until they receive a report from Hong Kong. According to official sources, Chen Jitang did ask the Hong Kong government to detain the two rebel ships. Jiang Xiyuan and others are still in prison. The authorities have also arrested several more people, reportedly related to the Dapeng Bay case. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Forty naval cadets on the Haiqi and Haishen are currently detained by the rebels of the two ships as a guarantee for the safety of Jiang Xiyuan's life. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) It is heard that the Navy Department will soon publish an article explaining the course of negotiations between Nanjing and the commanders of the Haiqi and other ships. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The strange cruiser encountered by the Haishen and Haiqi outside Hong Kong yesterday sailed into the harbor after midnight. Everyone saw that it was the newest cruiser in the Chinese fleet, the Ninghai. This ship was ordered by the Navy Department to come here to escort the Haiqi and other two ships north. Chen Jiliang, Vice Minister of the Navy Department, and British consultant to the Navy Department, Morse, are both on the Ninghai. Ninghai crew members told reporters that they had ordered the Haiqi and Haishen to return to Hong Kong and wait for orders after the rebel ships had contacted the Central Government. The Ninghai Line will accompany them north within a few days. The Ninghai was originally patrolling in Xiamen and was later ordered by Nanjing to come to Hong Kong to clean up the two escaped ships. At the same time, two other Nanjing warships, the Haichou and Hairong, also sailed to a bay several miles from Hong Kong. In total, there are six Nanjing warships near Hong Kong, including the Tongji. It is not yet known what mission the Tongji has after entering the harbor yesterday. It is speculated that the Tongji came here to report the actions of the two rebel ships to the warships guarding outside the harbor via radio. The commanders of the two ships, in talks with Reuters interviewers, confirmed the story of the Ninghai firing cannons. It is said that Chen Jiliang raised a signal after firing a cannon warning, and the two ships immediately sailed back to Hong Kong to await orders. Their relationship with Nanjing remains harmonious. According to the Englishman guarding the Waglan Lighthouse, the Ninghai fired a total of twelve cannons, and the escaped ships also returned fire. Nanjing can now ask the Hong Kong government to return the two ships through diplomatic channels. At the same time, one British submarine and one destroyer had all personnel who had been granted shore leave recalled, and another British destroyer sailed to Kowloon Bay to monitor the two ships and prevent anyone from landing. The sailors on the two ships are now obviously divided, and some have detained Chen Hao, the commander of the Haiqi, hoping to use him as a hostage to exchange for Jiang Xiyuan, who is being detained in Guangdong. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Japanese Consulate here denies rumors that naval rebels will sell the Haiqi and other two ships to the Japanese. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

(London) Reuters has learned that the British authorities will continue to treat the Haishen and Haiqi as part of the Chinese fleet until the British government receives a note from the Nanjing government declaring them as rebel ships. (13th Reuters Dispatch)

Strange Aircraft Suddenly Scouts in Yulin 5

Yulin A strange aircraft suddenly appeared here at 10:00 AM today. The aircraft was silver-gray and circled and scouted over the city of Yulin for about fifteen minutes before flying southeast. (21st Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) According to a semi-official message from Yulin, northern Shaanxi, today, a strange aircraft appeared in the sky over the city yesterday morning. The aircraft was gray and flew for about fifteen minutes before heading southeast. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Two Japanese aircraft, No. 126 and No. 128, from the Tianjin East Bureau Airport flew south along the Beiping-Hankou Railway to Baoding and south along the Tianjin-Pukou Railway to Dezhou at 8:00 AM and 9:30 AM on the 22nd, respectively, for low-altitude reconnaissance. They returned to Tianjin in the afternoon. (22nd Dispatch)

Sakai and Others to Visit Chahar Province for Investigation 6

(Beiping) After holding a headquarters meeting in Changchun, the Japanese Kwantung Army sent Sakai, Hamada, and others to inspect Beiping, Tianjin, and other places. After arriving in Shanhaiguan, Sakai and his party of four met with Iwai to convey the intentions of the Japanese Kwantung Army regarding the Hebei and Chahar incidents. Iwai, Matsuda, and others have now gone to Tianjin, and Sakai and his party are scheduled to come to Beiping and Tianjin in the next day or two. They will also visit Chahar Province to investigate the truth of the Zhangbei incident and the Dushikou incident. After the mission is completed, they will return to Changchun via Chahar and Rehe to report. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Lieutenant Colonel Kazu, the head of the China Section of the Japanese General Staff, is scheduled to arrive in Tianjin from Osaka on the 23rd to inspect the situation in Beiping, Tianjin, and the demilitarized zone, and then go to Chahar to investigate before returning to Japan via Rehe. (22nd Dispatch)

Reassignment of Magistrate of Zunhua and Miyun Counties 7

(Tianjin) According to a telephone call from Baoding, the Provincial Government believes that the magistrate of Zunhua and Miyun counties is important. On the 21st, it announced the transfer of Zhao Congyi, the magistrate of Yutian County, to the position of magistrate of Yunhua County, the transfer of He Huangxian, the magistrate of Huairou County, to the position of magistrate of Yutian County, and the appointment of He Houjing as the magistrate of Huairou County. They were ordered to take office immediately and expedite the post-disaster relief work in the counties. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Liu Guanggan, the deputy director of the Hebei Provincial Security Office, resigned. The Provincial Government appointed Liu Zhongji to replace him. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Four thousand special police officers from the war zone, who were surplus after the reorganization, are scheduled to depart from Caicun, Cangxian, to Baoding next week to maintain public order. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Rotation of US Troops Stationed in Tianjin 8

(Tianjin) Two hundred US soldiers from Tianjin left for Qinhuangdao by train on the evening of the 21st to board ships to return to the United States. The army is being rotated, and a new army has arrived from the Philippines, with another batch en route. (22nd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) One hundred and sixty-five US soldiers from Tianjin went to Qinhuangdao on the 22nd for field exercises. (22nd Dispatch)

Umezu Flies to Beiping and then Secretly Inspects Various Locations 9

(Tianjin) Umezu, the commander of the Japanese army in Tianjin, took a plane from Dongjuzi Airport along the Beining Railway to Beiping at 8:00 AM on the 22nd with his entourage and adjutants, and then transferred from Beiping to Miyun, Qian'an, and along the Great Wall, before turning east through Yulin and Tangshan, returning to Tianjin at 1:00 PM in the afternoon, to inspect the situation in the various locations. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Tianjin) At 7:00 AM on the 22nd, Umezu, the commander of the Japanese Garrison Army in Tianjin, and his staff officer Tangxie and adjutant Otake? departed from Dongjuzi Airport on a No. 23 giant light reconnaissance aircraft and took off, reconnoitering along the eastern section of the Beining Railway and Pingyu Road, and reconnoitering for a long time over Yangcun, Langfang, Junliangcheng, and Beiping. They then turned to the areas of Shanhaiguan, Tangshan, Tanggu, Miyun, Wangtian, Qian'an, and the demilitarized zone near the Great Wall for low-altitude reconnaissance, and returned to Tianjin at 11:00 AM, landing again at Dongjuzi. (22nd Dispatch)

Two Japanese Warships Left Tianjin Yesterday 10

(Tianjin) The Japanese destroyer Kudzu No. 2 raised anchor at 8:00 AM on the 22nd and sailed down from the Tianjin British Concession pier, arriving at Tanggu at 10:00 AM and leaving the port at 3:00 PM to return to Lushun. (22nd Dispatch)

Tianjin Municipality Placed Under the Jurisdiction of the Beiping Political Readjustment Committee 11

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan has announced that Tianjin Municipality is directly under the Executive Yuan. Regarding the issue of management, the Executive Yuan decided to follow the precedent of the Beiping and Qingdao municipalities and place it under the jurisdiction of the Executive Yuan's Political Readjustment Committee stationed in Beiping. The National Government has approved this. (22nd Dispatch)

China's Representative Expected to be Elected to the League of Nations Council 12

(Nanjing) The 18th session of the League of Nations General Assembly will be held in Geneva in the first week of September. China's representatives will be Yan Huiqing, Ambassador to the Soviet Union, Gu Weijun, Ambassador to France, and Guo Taiqi, Ambassador to the United Kingdom. At this meeting, many countries advocated that China should be elected as a council member to strengthen the League of Nations and avoid the regret of having no Far Eastern representative on the council. It is expected that there will be no more twists and turns in China's election as a council member this year. (22nd Dispatch)

Beiping Municipal Government and Others Agree on Measures to Stabilize Finance; 4 Million Loan IOUs Pledged for Cash Relief 13

(Beiping) The Beiping Municipal Government sent personnel to meet with the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Bankers Association, and the Silver and Money Industry Association to hold a meeting to discuss concrete measures to stabilize finance. As a result, it was decided that the Silver and Money Industry Association would pledge 4 million yuan in loan IOUs to the Bankers Association for 2 million in cash for turnover. From then on, Beiping's finance could return to its original state and become more consolidated. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) After the Beiping Municipal Government issued a notice strictly prohibiting rumors and disturbing finance, the Criminal Investigation Team of the Public Security Bureau arrested five people on the 22nd who refused to use the banknotes of a certain bank, and also arrested nine criminals who took the opportunity to disrupt finance, and sent them to the bureau for interrogation. In addition, Wei Zongshu and other 14 representatives of the creditor group of the Jucheng Yuan Silver Company went to the Municipal Government to petition on the afternoon of the 22nd. Yuan Liang sent Section Chief He Yuanhan to meet them on his behalf and gave satisfactory answers to the creditor group's requests to audit the company's accounts and protect the interests of creditors. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Beijing Public Works Bureau Pays Attention to Flood Control Matters in Beijing 14

(Nanjing) The Beijing Public Works Bureau has decided to follow the provisions of the flood control outline decided by the Yangtze River Conservancy Conference for flood control matters in Beijing. According to the outline, the flood control period begins when the river level reaches 5.5 meters on the Customs gauge, which will be managed by the local government. The dangerous period begins when the river level reaches 7.25 meters, and the Central Government will be requested for assistance at any time. It is also stipulated that the Sewerage Engineering Office of the bureau will comprehensively plan and formulate measures, connect with the Customs, and forward the daily water level records for reference. (22nd Dispatch)

Implementation of Income Tax to be Reasonably Postponed 15

(Nanjing) The implementation of income tax will be reasonably postponed, for a period of one or two months, depending on the progress of preparations. According to an official from the ministry, income tax is better than other taxes. Based on the country's expenditures and the domestic industrial and commercial situation, it can generate an annual revenue of 20 million yuan. However, this tax is still a new initiative in China. During this trial period, efforts will be made to seek the support of merchants and the military. Therefore, the revenue for the 24th year is only projected to be 5 million yuan. (22nd Dispatch)

Cantonese Silver Falls in Price; Authorities Crack Down on Speculation 16

(Guangzhou) The authorities have now decided to take strict measures to crack down on speculative activities that cause the price of provincial silver to fall, as the authorities believe that the recent fall in the price of provincial silver is entirely manipulated by speculators. It is heard that the managers of several local banks have been summoned by the Department of Finance to explain their reasons for purchasing large amounts of Hong Kong dollars. Today, the premium on Hong Kong dollars has fallen slightly. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

Heavy Rains in Wuhan for Several Days 17

(Hankou) There have been heavy rains in Wuhan for several days. On the 22nd, there was torrential rain all day, with water accumulating in the city streets and the river rising continuously, and the situation is gradually becoming serious. (22nd Dispatch)

Current Affairs Commentary

The Future of Anglo-American Cooperation 18

— Heng

British Prime Minister Baldwin stated last month that if Britain and the United States could cooperate, it would be the most effective guarantee of world peace. This statement is indeed accurate. The talk of Anglo-American cooperation has been ongoing for a long time, but its realization seems yet to come. Tracing back to the Manchurian Incident, Stimson of the United States requested joint action from Britain. After the London Naval Preliminary Talks last year, there was a tendency for Anglo-American cooperation. Since this spring, this atmosphere has become even more pronounced. For example, Lytton's visit to the United States emphasized the necessity of Anglo-American cooperation, and General Smuts of South Africa also stated at the same time that Anglo-American cooperation is indispensable. These arguments often rise and fall with the Far Eastern situation. Whenever the situation becomes tense, the call for cooperation suddenly becomes loud, and when the situation eases, the atmosphere of cooperation subsides. Therefore, although the intention is good, it does not help the facts. Recently, with the events in North China, Britain and the United States have again discussed using the Nine-Power Treaty to deal with the situation, but so far there has been no action. What is the crux of this? It is indeed a question worth noting.

According to our observation, the reason why Britain and the United States only have empty intentions for cooperation and have been slow to take action is due to several reasons: First, the situation in Europe, where France and Germany are still in opposition, and Italy also has great ambitions, posing a threat to European peace at any time. With Europe unstable, Britain can hardly attend to other matters. Second, the purpose of Anglo-American cooperation is nothing more than to restrain Japan's actions. If Japan is not restrained, it will inevitably resort to war. However, such a war would provide the Soviet Union with an opportunity to develop, which is also not what Britain and the United States desire. Therefore, if Britain and the United States do not have a firm grasp on controlling Russia, they will certainly not want to offend Japan. This kind of fear of Russia is especially strong in Britain, because once the power of the Soviet Union expands, Britain's Asian treasure, India, will be the first to suffer a great threat. Third, the United States' currency devaluation has caused great losses to Britain, while Britain's delay in repaying war debts, which is tantamount to defaulting on debts, has also made the United States feel very unhappy, and they are deeply wary of repeating the mistakes of joining the war last time. These are all reasons why it is difficult for Britain and the United States to cooperate effectively.

Based on the above reasons, it can be seen that the key to Anglo-American cooperation lies in whether a collective peace system in Europe can be established, what measures Britain and the United States will take regarding the future expansion of Soviet power, and whether the economic relations between Britain and the United States themselves can be adjusted. According to recent foreign news reports, after the establishment of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement, Britain is still planning to proceed with the various conventions in the Anglo-French London Declaration of February 3 to promote a collective peace system in Europe. If European peace can be established, Britain's attention can be shifted to the Far East. Also, according to recent news, Britain and the United States are again brewing to convene an international monetary conference, and the economic relations between Britain and the United States may therefore have a chance of coordination. Is it then possible for Anglo-American cooperation to become a reality? However, what we should pay attention to is that even if Anglo-American cooperation is realized, it may not have the effect of eradicating Japanese power. Based on the current situation, the future of cooperation will at most push the collective peace system currently being implemented in Europe to the Far East, so that countries with interests in the Far East can participate together to restrain the free actions of any one country. Considering that the British are still maintaining friendly relations with Japan, and that American naval officers advocate taking a defensive policy against Japan, and that President Roosevelt has repeatedly warned the military not to take actions that would harm diplomatic relations, the weight of Anglo-American Far Eastern policy can also be understood.

Anglo-French Talks Successfully Conclude; Continue Cooperation to Stabilize the European Situation; Britain Promises France Guarantees on General Issues; There is Talk of Germany Rejoining the League of Nations 19

(Paris) The recent rift in Anglo-French cooperation: British Minister Without Portfolio Eden began his repair work today. After Eden arrived in Paris, he was hosted at a banquet by French Prime Minister Laval. Immediately after the banquet, naval armament talks began. Subsequently, Laval issued a statement as follows: "We have studied the naval agreement recently concluded between Britain and Germany with complete sincerity. Eden informed us of the reasons why the British government made this decision, and I reiterated the French government's reservations regarding this matter. The personal relationship between me and Eden is sufficient to prove the friendly nature of the talks. We also jointly studied various issues presented by the European situation to our two governments. We recognize the necessity for close cooperation between the two governments." During the discussions, the strong spirit of friendship expressed by both sides made people feel optimistic, feeling that the haze that had been secretly sown between Britain and France as a result of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement was about to dissipate. France still insists that the Western European Air Pact must be an indivisible whole with the Eastern European Pact and the Danube Pact. Some parts may be negotiated separately, but can only be established simultaneously. It is reported that Laval asked Eden whether Britain still adheres to this principle, as this was agreed upon by the two countries in London in February of this year. Britain at that time was especially willing to complete the Air Pact as soon as possible, without waiting for the resolution of the Central and Eastern European issues before doing so. Now it seems that Britain is not following this path. Eden replied that he must first consult with the government. Tomorrow, talks between the two sides will continue. (Reuters, 21st)

(London) British Minister Without Portfolio Eden, who is currently in Paris, has recently communicated with the British government by telephone and inquired about the opinions put forward by France. It is reported that the British government has indicated that it intends to give France certain guarantees regarding the Air Pact and the Naval Agreement. Regarding the Air Pact, Britain will never conclude a separate agreement with Germany unless all signatory countries of the Locarno Treaty participate. As for the establishment of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement, if France increases its naval shipbuilding, Britain should not use this as a reason to increase its warships. This point is also recognized by Britain. (Havas, 22nd)

(Paris) It was learned here today that Hitler has probably agreed to rejoin the League of Nations as an exchange condition for Britain's support for his rearmament. People here generally believe that Eden has stated this to Prime Minister Laval and regard it as part of the reason for Britain's signing of the naval agreement with Germany. It is heard that Eden, when talking with Laval, requested Laval to consider the following four suggestions: (1) The Western European countries should immediately conclude an air force convention, in which Germany may be included. (2) Eden summarized Hitler's concessions before the signing of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement. (3) Germany's rearmament has become a reality, and Britain's purpose is to try its best to curb it. Britain hopes that this move can stop the arms race in Europe. (4) Request that Britain, France, and Italy continue to cooperate. People generally believe that Eden has won another diplomatic victory and averted the crisis of a break between Britain and France. Although France initially expressed shock at Britain's signing of the naval agreement with Germany, it recognized that a door for negotiating German armament issues has now been opened. (National Telegram, 21st)

Laval's Declaration; Considering Ways and Means of Cooperation; Adhering to the Collective Peace System 20

(Paris) The Anglo-French talks ended at 3:15 pm today. British Minister Without Portfolio Eden will soon depart for Rome. When returning to his country from Rome, he will pass through Paris and meet with Prime Minister Laval again. According to reports, after Eden consulted with the British cabinet by telephone this morning, the future of the negotiations has become smoother. However, the British government believes that the issues raised by France are very serious in nature, so it must wait for the cabinet meeting to discuss them before making a concrete decision. After the Anglo-French talks ended, Prime Minister Laval issued a declaration, saying, "We have considered the various issues raised by the current international situation. We have also reviewed the Anglo-French Declaration of February 3 and discussed the ways in which the two governments can cooperate. We all believe that it is necessary to find practical ways to resolve the various issues raised in the London Declaration, as these issues are not only related to the two countries, but also to other countries in Europe." Laval continued to declare that the two governments will remain committed to the collective security policy. (Havas, 22nd)

(Paris) According to reliable sources, although Britain has invited French naval experts to London for talks, France does not intend to send experts to Britain, at least not for such talks at the moment. However, France will participate in the naval conference to be held at the end of this year. (Havas, 21st)

(London) The French government sent a note to the British government on June 17, raising some opinions on the Anglo-German Naval Agreement. It is learned that the British government has sent a note replying to France, which has been delivered to the French Ambassador to Britain, Corbin, for transmission to the French government. (Havas, 23rd)

The British Ambassador Asks Russia to Participate in the Meeting

(Moscow) The British Ambassador, Seeds, has informed the Soviet Russian Foreign Minister, Litvinov, of the results of the Anglo-German Naval Conference, and stated that Britain hopes that Russia will also participate in the naval conference, in order to complete the qualitative and quantitative disarmament. The British government will also notify the Soviet Russian government of the progress of negotiations with related countries at any time. Litvinov replied that he would report the British proposal to the People's Committee, and that the Soviet Union has ordered the Soviet Russian Ambassadors in London, Paris, and Rome to inform the governments of the stationed countries of their country's opinions on the naval issue and the air force convention issue. (National News Agency, 21st)

(Moscow) The bulletin of the Soviet Union's Heavy Industry Committee commented on the Anglo-German Naval Agreement, saying, "In any case, one thing is clear: no matter how the British Foreign Minister declares, the Anglo-German Naval Agreement has neither reduced naval armament nor consolidated European security." (Tass, 21st)

(Moscow) Pravda pointed out that the Anglo-German Naval Agreement will have even greater consequences for the entire international situation, saying, "The increase in German armaments will be used as an excuse for Britain to expand its navy. Therefore, the purpose of this agreement is indeed to initiate an arms race. This agreement is the last nail in the coffin of the idea of disarmament on land, sea, and air." (Tass, 21st)

British and German Representatives Discuss Shipbuilding Procedures

(London) The chief German naval representative, Ribbentrop, met with Foreign Secretary Sir Hoare again in the afternoon, and also met with Naval Minister Monsell and Chief of Naval Staff Chatfield. Generally, if British and German naval experts can finalize the German shipbuilding procedures within tomorrow, the German delegation will return to their country on Sunday. (Havas, 21st)

(Paris) The Times commented on the visit of the British Minister Without Portfolio Eden to Paris, saying, "The navy and the air force are most important to Britain. For the sake of Britain, they should be resolved first. This point is certainly understood by people. However, Germany's land armament is not only related to French security, but is also most important and related to the security of all countries on the continent. It is hoped that our British friends can also understand this point. The current British diplomatic policy is already incompatible with the cooperation policies of Stresemann and Geneva. We French feel particularly confused and uneasy. Eden, who has a clear understanding of the European situation, cannot be unaware of this." The Intransigeant also made a similar argument, saying that if Britain is consistent and truly hopes for cooperation between Britain and France, Eden's visit will certainly declare to France that Britain is willing to cooperate with France on all current international issues. Cooperation itself is not a problem. The problem lies in how to cooperate. If Britain cannot cooperate effectively with France, then France does not need to cooperate with Britain. Regarding this point, Eden has a clear responsibility to explain it. We will wait and see." (Havas, 21st)

(London) The newspapers are generally optimistic about the Anglo-French talks in Paris. The Daily Telegraph reported, "We have good reason to believe that there will be progress tomorrow night. So far, Britain and France have agreed on the wording of their response to the German memorandum. This German memorandum raises objections to the Franco-Russian mutual assistance treaty, saying that it conflicts with the obligations stipulated in the Locarno Treaty and requests that the signatory countries of the Locarno Treaty clarify it." The Times said, "After Prime Minister Laval of France finished talking with Minister Without Portfolio Eden yesterday, he said that the reservations put forward by France still exist. From this, it can be seen that the French government still believes that the Anglo-German Naval Agreement, whether in spirit or in words, is contrary to the united front of Britain, France, and Italy. Fortunately, Eden responded appropriately and was able to make a deep impression on the French side. The talks should be successful tomorrow." (Havas, 22nd)

(Berlin) The establishment of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement is considered here to be Germany's greatest diplomatic success and a new starting point for various international negotiations. People in the German Foreign Ministry strongly claim that this agreement is a great diplomatic victory, and the National Socialist Party believes that the procedure for achieving equal rights advocated in Hitler's speech on May 21 has been concretely recognized, and that the Anglo-German naval talks were handled single-handedly by Hitler's new confidant Ribbentrop. Therefore, Germany's rapprochement with Britain is also Hitler's personal success. Semi-officially, it is believed that Hitler's book "Mein Kampf" criticized Germany's naval policy before the war and advocated coordination with Britain. Now Hitler's idea has become a reality. Since Germany recognizes Britain's naval superiority, Britain can also reduce its intervention in Germany's attempts in Central Europe. The National Socialist Party is now discussing that Ribbentrop may go to Paris to find ways to conclude an agreement with France similar to the Anglo-German Agreement. (Havas, 21st)

The Abyssinian Question is Not Discussed

(Rome) The British Commissioner to the League of Nations, Eden, will arrive here tonight or tomorrow morning. According to reliable political sources, when Eden meets with Prime Minister Mussolini, it has been decided not to discuss the Abyssinian question. His mission is limited to contacting naval issues, that is, the new note recently submitted by the League of Nations on Abyssinia will also be shelved indefinitely, as the mediation committee is currently studying the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, and it is not appropriate to create additional complications. (National News Agency, 22nd)

(Paris) Eden's conversation with reporters proves that he and Laval did not mention the Abyssinian question. Moreover, from the comments of various newspapers, it can be seen that France does not want to give the impression of interfering in the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. This attitude of France is a direct result of the signing of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement and is also due to the repeated warnings from French newspapers to the authorities not to force Italy to withdraw from the League of Nations. Eden told reporters that after he returns to Britain from Rome, he will advocate negotiating the Italian-Abyssinian issue with France. (National Telegram, 22nd)

(Rome) Italy recently recruited 8,000 workers in Egypt, preparing to send them to work in Italian colonies in East Africa. This matter was prohibited by the Egyptian government authorities. Today, the Fascist newspaper here strongly attacked the United States, believing that this move by the Egyptian government was directed by Britain and was not out of the Egyptian government's own intention. (National Telegram, 22nd)

(Rome) A few days ago, some Abyssinians insulted the Italian flag outside a cinema in Addis Ababa. According to the Italian side, these people were members of the Abyssinian Air Force who tore off the Italian flag on the car of the First Secretary of the Italian Embassy and cursed the Italians. After the Italian Embassy negotiated with the Abyssinian government, the Abyssinian government formally apologized today. The Italian Embassy expressed satisfaction, but it still needs to see how the Abyssinian government punishes the criminals. (Reuters, 20th)

Lausanne According to the Lausanne Daily, European socialist parties plan to hold a conference to protest against Italy's conquest of Abyssinia. The meeting place may be in Switzerland. The newspaper said that if this news is confirmed, it is hoped that the Swiss authorities will prohibit it. (Havas, 22nd)

Changes in British Foreign Policy 21

(London) According to the Star, since Sir Hoare took office as Foreign Secretary, there will be important changes in British foreign policy and its methods. The most important ones are as follows: (1) Strive for reconciliation with Germany. (2) Cooperate with the United States. (3) Britain's attitude towards Japan's progress in China will no longer be as tolerant as before. As for diplomatic personnel, there will also be a large number of changes. Permanent Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs Vansittart will succeed Lindsay as Ambassador to the United States. The vacant Under-Secretary of State will be filled by the current Ambassador to France, Clerk. (Havas, 21st)

The Issue of Belgium and Russia Resuming Diplomatic Relations; Currently Only Informal Contacts 22

Brussels Belgian Prime Minister Theunis replied in writing to the questions of members of parliament today, saying that Belgium and the Soviet Union have not yet had formal negotiations on restoring diplomatic relations. However, regarding the issue of whether there have been informal negotiations, the Prime Minister stated that it was inconvenient to make any announcement, only saying that this was unavoidable. It is reported that Vandervelde, the leader of the Second International, is the de facto Prime Minister of Belgium at present. He recently discussed the issue of restoring Russian-Belgian diplomatic relations with Soviet Russian Ambassador Potemkin in France. However, Vandervelde requested that the Soviet Union first stop its communist propaganda that hinders the Belgian Socialist Party. The informal negotiations mentioned by Theunis may refer to this. (National Telegram, 22nd)

German-Austrian Economic Negotiations; May Even Discuss Political Issues 23

(Geneva) Councillor Gole of the Austrian Vienna Provincial Council is an influential figure in Austria. It is heard that he is currently in Berlin discussing economic issues, or even political issues, with the German authorities. (Havas, 22nd)

(Vienna) The German-Austrian Veterans Association, which has thousands of members, has been ordered to be disbanded by the government because it is a disguised organization of the National Socialist Party. After this, Austria will only have one veterans' organization, namely the Patriotic Association of Veterans. This association has joined the Patriotic League and has a close relationship with the government. (Havas, 21st)

Political Turmoil in Yugoslavia; Regent Calls for Leader of Croatian Party 24

Belgrade Prince Regent Paul received Maček, the leader of the Croatian opposition party, in the afternoon. The conversation lasted for one and a half hours. It is heard that the content of the conversation is extremely important. Since January 5, 1929, when former King Alexander ordered the abolition of the constitution, Maček has only come to the capital twice to confront the State Protection Court's accusation that he was suspected of endangering the country. In addition, Maček has never come to the capital to meet with government authorities. Now that the regent summoned Maček and inquired about him, it is not only a victory for the Croatian Peasant Party, but also a victory for the joint group of Croatian and Serbian opposition parties, as Maček is the leader of the opposition group. Maček declared to the Havas News Agency, "I am not speaking here on behalf of the Croatian nation, but on behalf of the opposition group." Maček also visited the Minister of the Army and Navy, Jevtić. According to general opinion, the new cabinet may be a nationally concentrated cabinet, with Stojadinović, the Minister of Finance of the Jevtić cabinet, serving as the Prime Minister, and cooperating with various old political parties. If not, a neutral cabinet may be organized, with General Jevtić serving as the Prime Minister, because the parties of the Croatian nation have not opposed Jevtić personally. However, according to Maček's declaration, the opposition cabinet, no matter how it is organized, will demand the restoration of civil liberties and legal guarantees, or even demand the adoption of a free and secret voting system to re-elect the parliament. (Havas, 21st)

Belgrade Maček, the leader of the opposition group, recently declared to a representative of the Havas News Agency, "In my conversations with Prince Regent Paul and Minister of the Navy General Jevtić, I sincerely stated what necessary measures should be taken to create a new situation and a new atmosphere, so that various domestic issues, especially the Croatian national issue, can be effectively resolved." In addition, Maček declared to other reporters, "In any case, we will never attend this session of the House of Representatives, but we are currently on the path to understanding." (Havas, 22nd)

Poland to Amend Election Law 25

Warsaw The current parliament will probably close on July 5. Before closing, the House of Representatives will discuss the draft parliamentary election law on June 25-27, and the result will definitely be passed. The draft stipulates the cancellation of the party candidate system and the abolition of the direct secret voting system. Therefore, the leftists have expressed their opposition. The Socialist Party has decided to strike for 24 hours in Warsaw and Lodz on June 25 to protest the draft election law proposed by the government party. There is also a similar strike in the Dombrowa mining area. The Socialist Party refuses to contact the Communist Party for joint action, but demands that the Communist Party take joint action to demand a general, secret, direct, and proportional election system. (Havas, 22nd)

Economic Decline in Austria; Suicide Rate Highest in Europe; Three Times Higher Than Before the War 26

(Vienna) According to the semi-official National Newspaper, Austria's suicide rate is currently the highest in Europe. Taking 100,000 people as a unit, the suicide rates of various countries last year were as follows: Italy 11, France 20, Germany 26, Czech Republic 34, Hungary 36, Austria 44. In Vienna alone, there are 2,000 attempted suicides each year, three times higher than before the European War. The newspaper believes that although Austria's economic difficulties are not unrelated to the increase in the suicide rate, the main reason seems to lie in the psychological and spiritual suffering of the Austrians. (National Telegram, 21st)

International Labour Conference Passes 40-Hour Work Week 27

(Geneva) The International Labour Conference today passed the 40-hour work week convention by a vote of 79 to 30. This convention expresses purely moral agreement on the principle of a 40-hour work week for various industries. Any signatory country does not therefore bear any responsibility. It is expected that regulations on a 40-hour work week for several industries, such as public works, steel construction, glass, and coal mines, will be submitted to the conference for discussion on June 24. (Reuters, 22nd)

Greek Army Minister Declares Inclination Towards Restoration 28

Athens The Greek Army Chief, Kondylis, who is currently a powerful figure in Greece, declared today that the republican system has so far failed to ensure internal stability in Greece, so he would be very happy if the restorationists could win in the future national vote. Kondylis has always been a republican, and his sudden change of attitude should give the restorationists a great boost. (National Telegram, 21st)

Paraguayan-Bolivian Peace Treaty Approved by Both National Assemblies 29

The Chaco Peace Protocol, signed in the capital of Paraguay this month on the 12th, in the capital of Argentina, has been approved by the upper and lower houses of the National Assembly on the 18th and 20th by voting and the government has announced its approval. (Havas, 21st)

The Chaco Peace Protocol, signed in the capital of Bolivia this month on the 12th, in the capital of Argentina, has been approved by the upper and lower houses of the National Assembly by voting today. (Havas, 21st)

International Chamber of Commerce to Meet in Paris Later This Month 30

(Paris) The International Chamber of Commerce will meet here from the 24th to the 29th of this month. According to general estimates, there will be 1,201 representatives from Europe, America, Australia, China, Japan, and India coming to participate, and most of them will be accompanied by their families. During their stay in Paris, their expenses are estimated to be about 4 million gold francs. (Havas, 22nd)

American and Italian Congressmen Initiate Movement to Raise Silver Prices; Plan to Jointly Petition the President 31

(Washington) Senator Thomas, leader of the silver faction in the Senate, stated today that he expects forty-six senators to sign a petition requesting President Roosevelt to increase silver purchases. Thomas is the chairman of the committee investigating the reasons for the government's slow pace of silver purchases and is currently drafting a memorandum to explain how increased silver purchases can revitalize commerce. (National Telegram, 21st)

(Washington) The Treasury Department announced today that it has collected a total of $1,024,000,000 in income tax to date. This is the first time since 1932 that income tax revenues have exceeded $1,000,000,000. The total revenue for this fiscal year is estimated to be around $4,000,000,000, while expenditures are $7,000,000,000. (National News Agency Telegram, 21st)

(Washington) According to a report from the Department of Commerce today, the total value of gold imported into the United States in the week before June 14th reached $124,984,627, of which $103,000,000 came from France. During the same period, silver imports totaled $2,779,033, compared to $1,698,860 in the previous week. Of the silver imported this time, $1,500,000 came from Mexico, $86,000 from the United Kingdom, and $258,000 from Hong Kong. (National Telegram, 21st)

(London) In the week ending June 19th, silver exports from the UK decreased by £87,000, while imports increased by £228,000. The total value of silver exported during the week was £137,000, including £11,000 to the United States, £48,000 to Turkey, and £25,000 to Bombay. The total value of silver imported was £782,000, including £456,000 from Japan, £39,000 from Soviet Russia, £26,000 from Australia, £24,000 from France, £114,000 from Egypt, and £53,000 from Belgium. The net import was £645,000. (Reuters Telegram, 21st)

(New York) Gold worth $105,000 was shipped to Mexico in the past week. According to silver industry insiders, this is likely a transaction in which Mexico exchanged silver for gold. (Reuters Telegram, 21st)

(Washington) The House of Representatives today passed the report of the joint conference committee of the Senate and House regarding the naval appropriations bill. This report was already passed by the Senate on May 24th, so the bill will now be sent to the White House for the President's signature. The bill allocates $471,690,000, including an additional $11,690,000 that was voted for by the Senate to begin construction of the twenty-four new warships stipulated in the bill. (Reuters Telegram, 21st)

(Washington) The House of Representatives today passed the second supplemental budget bill proposed by the Appropriations Committee, and it is now submitted to the Senate for review. Funding for the construction of the new consulate in Shanghai is also included, with the committee allocating $750,000 for this purpose. The new building will be built on the Bund in Shanghai. This new construction will enhance the United States' position in China and will contribute to the American construction and manufacturing industries. (National Telegram, 21st)

(Washington) According to news from the White House today, President Roosevelt intends to amend the Constitution during the current congressional session to allow the central government to collect income tax on securities issued by states and local governments in the future, and to allow state and local governments to collect income tax on securities issued by the central government in the future. As for the situation regarding other new taxes, there is currently no change, as no one can definitively determine whether President Roosevelt wants to implement them during the current congressional session. Most Democratic leaders favor waiting for the next congressional session, but this is contingent on President Roosevelt's stance. (Reuters Telegram, 21st)

(Washington) According to private speculation, the Public Utility Holding Company Act proposed by the government, which advocates abolishing holding companies, may not be passed by the House of Representatives, as it is estimated that the number of affirmative votes is about forty votes short of the required number. At the same time, the House Interstate and Foreign Commerce Committee, disregarding President Roosevelt's intentions, has passed the subcommittee's report actively amending the original bill and will submit it to the full House. Organized public utility companies continue to attack this bill, and recently issued an article stating that although the original bill has been amended, it will ultimately destroy private business and be nationalized. (Reuters Telegram, 21st)

(Washington) Senator Tydings today advised Philippine Resident Commissioner Guvera to submit a request for $23,000,000 to the Senate Appropriations Committee. This amount is equivalent to the loss suffered by the Philippines due to the devaluation of the dollar. The House Appropriations Committee yesterday refused to include this request in the supplemental budget bill. Guvera hopes that the Senate will support this move and that the House will pass this request during reconsideration. When the House Appropriations Committee refused to include this request in the supplemental budget bill, it stated that the United States has taken good care of the interests of the Philippines, and that there is no sufficient reason to acknowledge this request. It should be known that from 1898 to 1935, the United States spent nearly $850,000,000 on the Philippines. (National Telegram, 21st)

Sino-French Vietnamese Trade Agreement Passed by the French Chamber of Deputies 32

(Paris) The government submitted a draft law to the Chamber of Deputies requesting ratification of the Special Agreement on Commercial Relations between France, Vietnam, and the bordering provinces of China, signed in Nanjing on May 16, 1930, and the appendix to that agreement signed on May 4 of this year. This bill has been passed by the Chamber of Deputies. During the discussion, Colonial Minister Roland delivered a speech stating that the Sino-French Vietnamese Treaty had been hoped for by all parties for a long time and is now fortunately established. The content of the treaty is quite beneficial to France. "Although we treat China with the lowest tax rates and other benefits, China also grants us preferential treatment for smokeless anthracite from Tokyo and rice produced in Vietnam. These two products will be easier to sell to China in the future." Roland also said that the total weight of goods shipped from France to China in 1925 and 1926 was less than 700,000 tons, while last year alone it reached 667,000 tons. (Havas Telegram, 21st)

Japan's Seiyukai Party Decides on Four Major Policies; Rejects Senior Statesmen's Alliance; Initiates National Movement Immediately 33

(Tokyo) As a result of yesterday's meeting of the Seiyukai Party's Provisional Executive Council, it was decided to follow the spirit of President Suzuki's guidance and traditional spirit, and to pass four major active policies: "Balance between military and agriculture," "Establishment of independent diplomacy," "Establishment of responsible politics," and "Rejection of the organ theory and clarification of the national essence." It was also decided that the party's attitude would be to reject the negative, defensive guiding spirit of the senior statesmen's groups that contradict these policies. After obtaining the approval of the Executive Council on the 27th, the specific strategies will be handed over to the Policy Research Council and other agencies. At the conference to be held in Osaka, Tokyo, and Sendai in late next month, President Suzuki will declare this intention to the world through speeches and declarations, and a major national movement will be launched. (Den-tsu Telegram, 22nd)

(Tokyo) Since his return to Tokyo, Seiyukai elder statesman Kunisuke Okazaki met with influential figures in the party last night to discuss the issue of party rejuvenation. However, there was no specific plan, and President Suzuki did not acknowledge the need for a rejuvenation strategy, deciding to develop the party's traditional and proactive policies under his own guidance. As a result, the elders' meeting, which had been planned for a while, was deemed unnecessary and dissolved. The result of the recent meetings was to avoid misleading the world into thinking there was a determined solution. (Den-tsu Telegram, 22nd)

Italian Female Aviator Sets New Women's Aviation Altitude Record 35

(Rome) Italian female aviator Negrone today flew her plane to an altitude of 39,500 feet, about seven and a half miles, setting a new world record for women's aviation altitude. Four days ago, French female aviator Hilsz flew to an altitude of 36,660 feet, setting a new record. Today, Negrone exceeded Hilsz's altitude by 2,840 feet, thus taking the record. International Commercial Telegram – Reuter's Special Commercial Report, June 22nd – 82

Gold and Silver

London gold price today is 141 shillings and one penny, a decrease of one penny.

London silver market spot price is 32 pence 225, futures are 32 pence 4375, an increase of one eighth seven five. Indian, Chinese, and speculators bought and then resold.

Mount Lyell silver futures prices today were quite mixed. September futures opened with some falling 40 pounds, some rising 15 pounds, quite inconsistent.

Exchange Rates

The Anglo-American London foreign exchange market was quite active today. The Anglo-American exchange rate opened at 4 dollars 9 and 3/875 cents, lower by one and a quarter than yesterday's US-UK closing price. There was no change before noon. At noon, it rose by zero six two five, and the closing price fell back by zero six two five, remaining at 4 dollars 9 and 3/875 cents.

The Anglo-French exchange rate opened at 74 francs 59, the same as yesterday's closing price. Within the first hour, it rose by six pounds, reaching 74 francs 65. At noon, it fell by two pounds, reaching 74 francs 63. This price remained unchanged until the close.

Cotton and Wheat

The New York cotton market opened without excitement this morning, and prices remained almost unchanged. The market showed a slight upward trend. Reports of unfavorable weather and poor cotton crops in the western cotton belt are gradually increasing.

Chicago wheat is expected to have good weather, and the opening price fell slightly. The same is true for coarse grains. The market situation is now entirely dominated by weather news, and prices are easily affected. Prices continued to fall after the opening due to a lack of interest from the industry.

Liverpool wheat continued to be stable today. At 1 PM, the July futures price was 5 shillings 4 and one eighth pence, an increase of two fifths.

Securities

The panic in New York caused by President Roosevelt's new tax proposal has temporarily subsided. Therefore, the stock market opened today with a renewed upward trend from yesterday. Most stocks have risen in price. The House Interstate Commerce Committee has passed a report on the Public Utility Holding Company Act with positive revisions, and it will be submitted to the House after slight modifications. This is also favorable news for the securities market. It is also reported that the cancellation clause in the Holding Company Act will fail due to a lack of forty votes when it is voted on at a later date. The improvement in securities this morning is also due to this reason. The opening average price of the Dow Jones 30 industrial stocks was 119.87, up thirty-nine pounds.
