Child Falls Ill and Seeks Help from Buddha: Ignorant Woman Treats Life as Child's Play; Detestable Immortal repeatedly Frauds Money 137

Shen Miaosheng, a local resident, is 41 years old. He lives at No. 39 Chengqing Lane, Bair Road, Taiping Bridge, French Concession. He runs a tofu shop for a living. His wife, Lai, is about the same age as Shen. They have a son named Xiaomao, who is three years old this year. Last month, Xiaomao suddenly fell ill with measles. After seeing a doctor and taking medicine, he recovered. However, at the beginning of this month, the child's illness suddenly relapsed with chills and fever. The fever was very high and did not subside for a long time. The child's mother, Shen Lai, heard from a neighbor that there was an Immortal Hall at No. 11 Ziyang Lane, No. 64 Lafayette Road, that could cure illnesses. Taking their Immortal prescription was very effective. Lai, being a woman,

Lacking Knowledge

is usually very superstitious. She often heard people say that there was a Five Saints Bodhi Temple, and wealthy families often came by car to ask for Immortal prescriptions and burn incense. On the morning of the 3rd of this month, she took incense, candles, and ingots and went there piously to ask for an Immortal prescription. When she arrived, Lu Xiangtian, a Jiangbei Yancheng native who called himself an Immortal (nicknamed Xiaoliuzi, 34 years old), came out to greet her. He told her to quickly buy several walnuts in preparation for obtaining an Immortal pill. Lai immediately turned around and went out, bought twenty walnuts from a nearby dried goods store, and then went to the Immortal Hall to register, paying six jiao in small coins and ten copper coins, and handing over all the walnuts

To the Immortal

Lu Xiangtian held the walnuts in front of the Five Saints Bodhisattva and silently chanted a mantra. When Lai was not paying attention, he took out a walnut he had hidden in his sleeve and mixed it with the walnuts Lai had handed over. Unexpectedly, his technique was not skillful, and Lai saw it from the side. However, she still firmly believed that the Bodhisattva was efficacious and did not expose Lu's trick at the time. After Lu recited strange incantations, he picked out the walnut he had put in, smashed the shell with a hammer, and several pills made of incense ash rolled out. He handed them to Lai to take back and give to the child to swallow, saying that the illness would be cured immediately. Lai did not consider the consequences and took them home, giving them to her son as instructed. But

Her Son's Illness

not only did not improve, but worsened. Two days later, she went to the Immortal Hall again to beg the Immortal Lu Xiangtian to ask the Bodhisattva to save her son's illness. Lu took the opportunity to tell her to pay fifteen yuan in foreign currency to buy tin foil and sandalwood for praying to the gods. She paid the amount as requested. After several days, her son's illness still did not improve. On the 9th of this month, Lai went to beg for an Immortal pill again. Lu told her to buy a special, thicker incense stick for use. She went to all the incense and candle shops but could not find this special incense. She told Lu this, and Lu claimed that he had this kind of incense for sale, but it had mantras recited on it and required a fee of twenty yuan in foreign currency. At that time, Lai was anxious to cure her son's illness as soon as possible, so she ignored everything and

Did Not Guard Against Fraud

and paid the amount in full. Lu took the incense, lit it in front of the Buddha, and chanted incantations. When the incense burned to more than half, a pre-hidden mud pill fell out. Lu claimed that this pill was an Immortal pill bestowed by the Bodhisattva, picked it up, and handed it to Lai to take back and give to her son to swallow. However, her son, Xiaomao, had taken pills that had no effect several times and had not received proper medical treatment, so his illness became more dangerous. The child's father, Shen Miaosheng, learned that his wife was superstitious about clay and wood idols and had been defrauded of money, causing the illness to be delayed and not cured. He sent Xiaomao to the Red Cross for treatment and reported to the French Concession police, accusing Lu of scheming

To Defraud Money

and requesting an investigation. The police chief approved the request and sent detectives to the Immortal Hall at No. 11 Charity Lane on the afternoon of the day before yesterday to arrest the Immortal Lu Xiangtian. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Special Second Court for questioning. After Judge Qiu Huan Ying asked the defendant about his age and place of origin, Lu stated that he was 34 years old, from Jiangbei, and lived at No. 11 Charity Lane. He owned a woodworking shop at No. 163 Dongzilaihuo Street and had not committed any crimes before. (According to records, Lu was accused of embezzling the money of a Buddhist nun last year and was beaten and injured when he demanded it back. He was detained by the French Concession police and sent to court. The result was an acquittal.) Yuan Jiahuan, a lawyer from the Police Department, stated that the defendant was detained on charges of fraud and obtaining property. The police had not yet investigated the case and requested that the

Defendant Be Detained

and the case be investigated at a later date. Then the plaintiff Shen Miaosheng testified about his wife being deceived due to their child's illness, and said that the child's condition was still dangerous and might not be saved, and he had hired a lawyer to represent him in the case and filed an attached civil suit. The judge listened to the testimony and told Shen, "This is because your own brains are too muddled in treating the illness. In this world, no one has died because of this." He then questioned the defendant Lu Xiangtian, who said that Shen's wife came to ask him to pray to the Bodhisattva on her behalf and he had not taken any money from her. He also hired lawyer Zhu Dianqing to defend him. The judge then told Lu, "You are praying to the Bodhisattva for people to cure illnesses. You must know that this is not saving people, but harming people!" At this point, the court adjourned the case to the 16th for further questioning and ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody.

Public Bus Driver and Ticket Seller in Zhabei Severely Beaten by Three Foreigners 142

According to a message from the China Business Public Bus Company, around 7:00 PM on the 21st of this month, China Business Company's Route 5, Bus No. 4936, was returning from the Municipal Government to the North Station when, upon arriving near the Kailin Company on West Tiyuhui Road, driver Gao Sanhou suddenly stopped the bus to avoid pedestrians in front of the vehicle. As a result, three foreigners in their private car, who were approaching from the opposite direction, also stopped. Infuriated, they severely beat both the bus driver and the ticket seller. The company, seeing that its employees had been beaten for no reason and that the bus's progress had been delayed, sent a letter to the North Station Branch requesting that the perpetrators be investigated. The letter is recorded as follows: Respectfully, our company's Transportation Section Chief Shi Guanfen reported that on the afternoon of the 21st of this month at 7:50 PM, driver Gao Sanhou, No. 72, was driving Public Bus No. 4936 along West Tiyuhui Road from south to north. Upon reaching the vicinity of the Kailin Paint Company, he turned the wheel slightly and immediately stopped to avoid pedestrians in front of the vehicle. At that time, a private car with city license No. 1430, a black license plate, (the owner of the car is reportedly an American, Mr. R.N. Harris) was approaching from the opposite direction and also stopped. Unexpectedly, three foreigners emerged from the vehicle. One of them climbed into the driver's seat through the eastern window, while the other two boarded the bus, and together they severely beat driver Gao Sanhou, No. 72, and ticket seller Pan Linyun, No. 58. As a result, the driver suffered a severe head injury, and the ticket seller also sustained head injuries. After finishing the beating, the three foreigners immediately returned to their private car and drove away. However, there were no police officers present at the time, and there was no way to call for help. They endured the pain and recorded the license plate number of the private car. They reported the incident to the Qujiaqiao Police Station. Upon hearing the news, the company reported it to your bureau and sent the two injured employees to Renji Hospital in the Concession for treatment. According to Gao Sanhou's medical certificate No. 5538, he needs to stop working for five days and visit the hospital for eight days before he can fully recover. The ticket seller's medical certificate No. 5537 states that he needs to be treated for one day. According to the report, the company's driver and ticket seller were severely beaten by the three foreigners for no reason. This is a violation of justice and an infringement on people's livelihood. We are sending this letter along with the two medical certificates, requesting your bureau to forward it to the superiors to investigate the perpetrators associated with city license No. 1430 and to give the three foreigners a warning and compensate the driver and ticket seller for all the losses they suffered from the injuries in order to maintain the safety of the people and protect commerce. We would be deeply grateful.

Nurse Quarrels with Sister and Takes Poison 147

Chen Mengai, a young woman from Chaozhou, 22 years old, works as a nurse at Pushen Hospital in Zhabei. Yesterday afternoon at about 3:00 PM, she had a quarrel with her sister over a trivial matter. Afterwards, feeling angry, she went alone to the Xinxudongfang Hotel on Xizang Road and checked into room 258, where she secretly committed suicide by taking poison. Later, the tea attendant discovered her and sent her to Renji Hospital for treatment. It is said that she had taken a lot of poison and her life was in danger.

Tea Attendant Sentenced for Forcing a Young Girl 148

Zhang Laosan, a woman from Changzhou, owns a brothel at No. 230 Guangxi Road and keeps two prostitutes, Xu Cainu and Wang Fengying. Recently, she lured Zhang Jinhua, a 15-year-old girl from her hometown, to Shanghai, intending to force her into prostitution. Because Zhang Jinhua was still a virgin, Zhang Laosan took her to room 5010 of the Nanfang Hotel on Jiangxi Road on the 2nd of this month. The hotel's tea attendant, Lu Jinlin from Taicang, was paid two yuan by Zhang Laosan for Zhang Jinhua to have her 'cherry broken'. Because the girl struggled, she was accidentally injured in the urethra by Lu, causing continuous bleeding and unconsciousness. Zhang Laosan sent her to Renji Hospital for treatment. This was learned by Zhang Jinhua's mother, Zhang Li, who went to the hospital and made a scene. The Laoza Police Station was notified by the hospital, and detectives Zhang Yuanjing and Jiang Linxiang arrested Zhang Laosan and Lu Jinlin, along with the two prostitutes Xu Cainu and Wang Fengying. They were sent to the Special First Court for trial. Lawyer Ru Baoqi, relying on Articles 240, 246, 247, and 315 of the Criminal Law, filed charges against Zhang Laosan and Lu. After the interrogation was concluded, Feng Shide, the presiding judge, issued a sentence in the Third Criminal Court yesterday morning. Zhang Laosan was sentenced to three years of imprisonment for making a living by enticing women from good families to commit adultery for profit. Lu Quanlin was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment for injuring the girl. Zhang Jinhua was taken back by her mother, and the two prostitutes Xu and Er were sent to the Women and Children Relief Society to be sent back to their hometowns.

Yang Wei Sues for Cohabitation with His Wife 149

Yang Wei, a native of Nanjing at No. 485 Shanxi Road, is currently 20 years old. His father runs a store, and Yang assists in the store. In the autumn of the 23rd year of the Republic of China, he was introduced by a matchmaker and engaged to Jinling, a woman with the surname Zai from Suzhou. Jinling is twenty years old and beautiful. In October of that year, Yang held a formal wedding at the Yuandong Hotel on Xizang Road. Initially, the relationship between the two sides was harmonious. However, since the 16th day of the ancient lunar new year this year, Jinling suddenly took her clothes and ornaments and returned to her mother's home in Suzhou, claiming that she was going to celebrate the new year. Then, she suddenly went to her aunt's house at No. 2 Hekang Lane, Xintangjia Lane, and has been living there for four months without returning. Yang has asked his aunt to pick her up three times, but she has been refused. Yang has now hired lawyer Xu Jie to file a lawsuit with the First Special District Local Court, requesting that the defendant Jinling be ordered to cohabitate with him. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Qiao Wanxuan opened the seventh civil court for trial. Both the plaintiff and the defendant, along with their lawyers, appeared in court. According to the plaintiff Yang Wei, he requested cohabitation and had tried mediation, but it was unsuccessful, but there had been no maltreatment. The defendant's lawyer, Hu Fenglian, stated that the defendant was an old-fashioned woman who did not want a divorce, but if she were to cohabitate, the plaintiff should pay her a monthly allowance of 70 yuan in foreign currency. Judge Qiao advised both parties to reconcile, and the court adjourned the case to a later date for further investigation.

Accomplice in Murder Case Sentenced to Eight Months 150

Wang Xiaodi, a native of Ningbo, was attacked with an ax and seriously injured outside the Yijia Gate at No. 59 Bouton Road on March 15 at 9:15 AM. Xie Jingen, also a native of Ningbo, was arrested and sent to the First Special District Court for trial and sentenced to eight months of imprisonment. He confessed that his accomplice, Shen Jinfal (also a native of Ningbo), was at large. An arrest warrant was issued. On the 12th of this month, Chinese detective Hu Guangrong of the Hongkou Police Station arrested Shen on Parker Road and sent him to the Third Criminal Court for detention. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Shuzi came to court for interrogation. Wang Yaotang, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, stated that it was found that they had a feud over the sale of morphine and suspected that the victim Shen Xiaodi had informed the police, hence the attack. The defendant was being questioned on this basis. According to his confession, he went with the defendant to question Wang Xiaodi, which led to an argument. However, the defendant did use the ax handle to hit him. Questioned about this, the defendant's confession was evasive. Judge Jiang sentenced Shen Jinfal to eight months of imprisonment as a warning.

Tao Shirong Sentenced for Selling Counterfeit Money 151

Tao Shirong, a native of Yangzhou, has been unemployed and unable to make a living recently, and has been secretly selling counterfeit money in a tea house at No. 567 Xizang Road for profit. On the 15th of this month, this was discovered by Chinese detective Ni Jiagui of the Hongkou Police Station. That night at about 9:00 PM, he sent an informant to act as a customer, agreeing that each counterfeit 100 yuan bill would be sold for 25 yuan in genuine foreign currency. Detective Ni paid 50 yuan, ordering 200 of the one yuan bills, promising to deliver the remainder the next morning after acquiring them from a ringleader named Lao Peng on Wuding Road. When the arrest was made, another counterfeit one yuan bill was found in his brass basin straw hat, and he was sent to the First Special District Court for trial. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Shuzi continued the trial in the Third Criminal Court. Lawyer Yu Yaotang of the Public Works Department stated that the leader Lao Peng could not be apprehended during the adjournment. Recently, such cases have occurred frequently in both the Chinese and Concession areas. The harm to society caused by these people is countless, and heavy punishment is necessary to prevent others from imitating them. Questioned by the defendant, he confessed that Xu Hong and two other fugitives had framed him and that he had nothing to do with it. Judge Jiang said that the evidence was solid and that there was no room for evasion, and sentenced Tao Shirong to two years and six months of imprisonment in court. The number of days spent in detention before the judgment was confirmed would be used to offset the imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. The 101 counterfeit bills were confiscated and destroyed.

China Merchants Bureau: Jiahe Steamer Collides with Butterfield & Swire Mooring Buoy; Ship Owner Claims No Collision; Inspection Required 152

The China Merchants Bureau's Jiahe steamer, which had already suspended operations in Shanghai, was chartered to Xiamen. On the 20th of this month, the steamer returned to Shanghai from Xiamen. The ship entered the port at 9:00 AM, and when it arrived at Butterfield & Swire's B.&.S. North Beoy mooring buoy, there was a sudden rainstorm. The wind and waves struck the stern of the ship, causing it to collide with and damage the aforementioned buoy. According to the Jiahe's captain's report, he did not feel anything at the time, nor was there any damage. However, according to a letter from Butterfield & Swire, the buoy was damaged by the Jiahe, and the matter was reported to the Customs Marine Department. The Customs Marine Department has now sent a letter to the China Merchants Bureau, stating that if the buoy was indeed damaged in the collision, all repair costs should be borne by the Bureau. The China Merchants Bureau has also notified the insurance company, requesting them to send a surveyor to inspect the buoy. If the buoy is indeed damaged, they will arrange for repairs.

Xu Yu (age 29), a Nanjing woman residing at 198 Xujiahui Road, was walking along Route Haig yesterday afternoon when Zhang Lansheng, a local man riding a bicycle, came flying towards her. Xu Yu was unable to avoid him and was knocked to the ground. She is four or five months pregnant, and the impact caused a shock to the fetus, causing her extreme pain and fainting. Zhang Lansheng then took the injured woman to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment.

Literacy School Compendium 155

The Touqiao Agricultural Education Center and the Touqiao Farmers' Education Center recently established roadside education and field teaching. Roadside education is currently set up in two locations: the first at the Jiazaitel area of Chuan'an Township, suitably located along the Qin Emperor Road; the second at the Youcheqiao area, suitably located along the Yantang Road. Each location has two instructors, one team leader and one team member. Passersby are tested to see if they are literate. Those who are illiterate are taught. More than 400 people are taught each day. Field teaching is conducted on clear days. Teachers bring tools and guide people in the fields. In addition to literacy, common knowledge is also taught. To create an atmosphere of intense literacy, the center presented Shandong Wu Xun last night, performed by the Guangyi Society. Only literate people were allowed to be seated. Zhou Tielao, president of the Old Farmers' Association, also attended, making for a very grand occasion.

Sports News

Berlin World Games: New Hurdle Structure Announced; Game Tickets on Sale from July 1; Venue to be Completed in Full by May Next Year 168

(Berlin Dispatch) The 11th World Games, Berlin is actively preparing, sparing no effort. Regarding the new rules for hurdles, the General Assembly has officially announced its adoption. The German Ministry of the Army has also issued a welcome letter, welcoming athletes from all countries. The latest news is summarized as follows:

New Hurdle Structure

At this year's Stockholm International Amateur Athletics Federation meeting, regarding the hurdle issue, anyone who knocks down one or several hurdles will not have their results or qualifications canceled. However, in the past, when hurdles were knocked down, they often tripped runners' legs or fell onto the running tracks of others. The new hurdle rules will be used at next year's World Games. Therefore, the structure of the hurdles must be greatly changed. The new hurdle, as shown in the figure, is constructed of wood or steel bars. At both ends of a base, two columns stand upright. The ends of the columns are fitted with one or two horizontal bars that can be raised or lowered at will to meet the required height. During raising and lowering, a spiral can be used to make it stand firmly without falling. The total weight of the hurdle must be over 22 pounds. The horizontal bar must have a resistance of at least eight pounds to be knocked down. The height of the 110-meter high hurdle is 1.06 meters (formerly 1.067 meters). The height of the 200-meter low hurdle is 76.2 centimeters, and the 400-meter medium hurdle is 91.4 centimeters. The hurdle is 1.20 meters wide, and the base is 70 centimeters long. The upper horizontal bar is painted black and white.

Venue Completion Deadline

Due to the very good weather in May, work at the venue is being stepped up, with 2,300 workers. It is scheduled to be completed before May 1 next year. The large swimming pool and open-air theater can be completed by next autumn. The first completed field will be the hockey field.

Tickets on Sale

Tickets for various competitions will go on sale starting June 1. These tickets include track and field, swimming, boxing, equestrian, football, fencing, wrestling, weightlifting, hockey, handball, and gymnastics. Prices range from six to forty marks, with a total of 25 different types of tickets. Tickets for the opening ceremony on August 1 and the demonstration of baseball between the United States and Japan, and the closing ceremony on August 16, will be sold separately. Swimming Contest: China Youth Los to McLing, 36 to 33 169

The China Youth swimming team competed against the McLing team last night at the YMCA on Sichuan Road. McLing won first place in five of the eight events, while China Youth won three. In the end, McLing defeated China Youth by a margin of three points, with a score of 36 to 33. In addition, there were three public events. Shi Bogen set a new China Youth record in the 400-yard freestyle. Details are as follows:

China Youth Starts Strong, Then Declines: Last night, McLing was represented by nine athletes and fifteen supporters. China Youth had twenty-six athletes. In the initial events, China Youth scored points as if soaring upwards. At its peak, China Youth had 30 points, while McLing had 24. When the scores were announced, the cheers from the poolside were thunderous. However, in the underwater swimming and fancy diving events, China Youth only had Yu Rongji score points. McLing's score suddenly increased sharply. Going into the final fancy relay event, China Youth was only leading by three points. Unfortunately, China Youth suffered a crushing defeat in the final 120-yard relay and fancy diving events, and McLing surpassed them in total score.

Shi Bogen Sets Record: Among the public events, the 400-yard freestyle was the most rewarding. It required swimming twenty laps around the pool. The participants were Shi Bogen, Chen Shengji, He Yuedian, and Zhang Liangsheng. Shi's endurance was unmatched. Chen, He, and Zhang dropped out midway. Only Shi continued to swim, completing the race in an excellent time of 5 minutes and 19.5 seconds, breaking his previous record of 5 minutes and 36.6 seconds.

This Year's Middle School and Physical Education Teacher Training School Graduates' Joint Examination Begins Tomorrow 182

Over 5,000 students participating, held in 20 examination halls

The joint examination for graduates of middle schools and physical education teacher training schools in this city is scheduled to begin tomorrow for one day. Over 5,000 students will participate in the joint examination and re-examination, held in 20 examination halls. The following is a report on the details:

Number of Participants: A total of over 2,500 students from 67 high schools, over 3,000 students from 89 junior high schools, and 150 students from 5 physical education teacher training schools will participate in the high school joint examination. A total of over 5,600 students from 166 schools will participate. High school exams will be in 7 halls, with an additional hall for high school and junior high school re-examinations.

Examination Times: (1) High School Examination Times (same for re-examination): Foreign Language on the 24th from 9 AM to 12 PM, History from 1 PM to 3 PM, Biology from 3:45 PM to 4:15 PM, Mathematics on the 25th from 9 AM to 11 AM, Geography from 1 PM to 2:30 PM, Chemistry from 2:45 PM to 4:15 PM, Chinese Language on the 26th from 9 AM to 12 PM, Party Principles from 1 PM to 2 PM, Physics from 2:45 PM to 4:15 PM. (2) Junior High School Examination Times (same for re-examination): Foreign Language on the 24th from 9 AM to 12 PM, History and Geography from 1 PM to 2:30 PM, Biology from 2:45 PM to 4:15 PM, Mathematics on the 25th from 9 AM to 12 PM, Physics and Chemistry from 1 PM to 2:30 PM, Party Principles from 2:45 PM to 4:15 PM, Chinese Language on the 26th from 9 AM to 12 PM. (3) Physical Education Teacher Training School Examination Times: Principles of Physical Education, Physical Education Administration on the 24th from 9 AM to 12 PM, Introduction to Education from 1 PM to 2:30 PM, Soft Gymnastics from 2:45 PM to 4:15 PM, Human Anatomy and Physiology on the 25th from 9 AM to 12 PM, History and Geography from 1 PM to 2:30 PM, Party Principles from 2:45 PM to 4:15 PM, Chinese Language on the 26th from 9 AM to 12 PM.

Important Information for Examinees: (1) Examinees must strictly abide by the examination hall rules and all orders from the chief examiner and proctors. Violators will be punished according to the severity of the circumstances. (2) Each examination hall will ring the bell ten minutes before the start of the joint examination. Examinees should enter the hall immediately and be seated according to their admission ticket number to await verification. (3) Examinees must place their admission ticket on the table for the proctors to check at any time. (4) Each joint examination subject will have ten minutes before the end to prepare the end. (5) Examinees should rest in the designated resting place after leaving the examination hall, and should not walk around freely to obstruct order. (6) Examinees must carry their admission ticket with them during the joint examination period and must not lose it. It should be returned after all subjects have been examined. (7) Examinees are responsible for their own meals. Each examination hall provides tea. (8) Examinees are not allowed to bring any books, papers, or objects other than the stationery they will use into the examination hall. (9) After each subject is examined, each student must tear off the floating ticket on the examination paper and must not write their own name, secret name, or any other symbol on the examination paper. Violators' examination papers will be invalidated. (10) After each subject is examined, examinees should place the examination paper on the table for the proctors to collect. There is no need to hand it in. All test questions and drafts must be attached to the paper and returned, and must not be taken out of the examination hall.

Examination Hall Rules: (1) Examinees must enter the examination hall with their admission ticket before the prescribed examination time. Those who arrive more than five minutes late will not be allowed to enter and will be considered absent. (2) Examinees must bring a writing brush, inkstone, or pen, ink, and mathematics tools when entering the examination hall. Other items are not allowed to be brought in (except for pencils for writing, all other items cannot be used with pencils). (3) Examinees must be seated according to their admission ticket number and must not change seats. (4) Each examinee will only be issued one examination paper for each subject, and they cannot be exchanged. (5) Examinees must not ask questions, talk, look around, leave their seats, smuggle, plagiarize, or substitute for others during the examination. Violators will not be allowed to participate in the joint examination. If it is necessary to ask a question, they should raise their hand first. (6) If an examinee needs to leave the examination hall temporarily due to a special event, they should report to the proctor and obtain permission from the chief examiner before leaving. (7) Examinees must abide by the prescribed examination time and must not extend it. (8) After each subject has been examined, examinees should place the examination paper on the table for the proctors to collect. Examinees should leave the examination hall immediately. (9) Examinees must strictly abide by all orders from the chief examiner and proctors during the joint examination.

Finance: Guangdong Merchants Covering Short Positions, Gold Prices Soaring – Breaking Through the 800 Yuan Mark – Rising Twelve Yuan and Ninety Cents in Half a Day, Stakes Increase to Sixteen Thousand 190

The gold market has been steadily firm in recent days, and people's hearts are extremely excited. Yesterday, rumors of various bullish factors suddenly spread within the market, triggering a large number of buy orders. The short side was forced to close out positions in pain. Large traders widely bought to cover short positions, and the rise was so rapid that it broke through the 800 yuan mark. The morning began with the overseas silver market, where the British and Americans were flat. Large traders said that the United States and speculators had bought above the closing price of 0.625 after the market closed. The forward silver market in Monterrey was one to two cents higher. Exchange rates were slightly higher. London spot gold rose by one penny. The over-the-counter trading opened and immediately retreated to 86.7 yuan, and soon dropped to 5.5 yuan. Buyers took advantage of the low prices to become active and stabilized. The central bank's posted prices were announced, with both the British and Americans shrinking. The customs gold unit rose by one point and one tenth of a cent. The standard price for gold was posted at 843.2 yuan, and people's hearts were settled. After the opening, the market gradually recovered. Later, Guangdong merchants began to cover short positions, and rumors of inflating currency spread, fueling the rise. However, because HSBC's posted prices for both the British and Americans were flat, the long side cashed out. Although the rise occurred midway, there were many trades. The short side was already in a desperate situation, and retail investors had to scramble to buy bars, breaking through the 800 yuan mark and rising to 805 yuan. A major bank dumped shillings, and sellers took advantage of the high prices to become active, and the market retreated. Although Guangdong merchants strongly advanced, HSBC and China Merchants Bank repeatedly sold foreign exchange, the foreign exchange market loosened, and arbitrage activity increased. The government bond market did not rise, people's hearts calmed slightly, and selling pressure increased, retreating to within the 100 yuan mark, and the fall was close to the previous yuan. Guangdong merchants continued to advance, and foreign exchange also continued to stabilize due to the strong buying of China Merchants and Guangdong merchants. The supply side was no match. Afterwards, the market repeatedly broke through the 800 yuan mark. However, the banks' selling pressure was strong, and there were many trades after the rise, fluctuating around 800 yuan. Later, Reuters and Associated Press reported that Senator Thomas of the American Banking Association stated that 46 people in the Senate had jointly requested the government to increase the silver purchase policy. Although slightly weak, the short side's buying was still strong, and the market ultimately remained above the 800 yuan mark. The market situation in the first half of the day was extremely strong. If the banks had not taken the opportunity to suppress prices, the rise would not have been limited to this level. The market situation in the first half of the day is recorded below:

Foreign Exchange Supply and Demand Both Strong: Banks Aggressively Sell, Chinese Merchants Vigorously Buy; Forward Months Tighter, Swap Rates Slightly Closer 191

According to yesterday's foreign dispatches from London, the major rate and nearby rate both narrowed to 1.879. It was said that after the market closed, the price remained above 0.0625 on the bid, with American and speculative buyers entering the market. The New York silver price remained unchanged. Forward silver in Montreux rose by 1 to 2%, not uniformly. London spot gold rose by one penny. Sterling rose against the dollar by 0.25. Sterling fell against the French franc by 3 points. The dollar rose against sterling by 0.625. The dollar rose against the French franc by 0.25. The exchange market opened in the morning with recent selling prices: Sterling at 1 shilling, 7 pence, 625 points, and the US dollar at 40.375 yuan, both down by half compared to the previous close. After the opening, the market loosened slightly, but because the Central Bank's posted rate was revealed, sterling narrowed by 0.25 and the dollar fell by 0.25. Customs gold rose by 1 fen and 1 li, stabilizing the sentiment of Chinese merchants. Rumors of positive news resurfaced, and Chinese merchants suddenly rushed to cover their short positions. Due to a lack of supply, although the HSBC's posted rate was flat, the process was extremely tight again and again. Later, the Central Bank took advantage of the high prices to release shillings, slightly stabilizing the situation. HSBC, the Central Bank, and others worked diligently to release US dollars and shillings, gradually easing the market. However, with the vigorous buying of Cantonese banks and Chinese merchants, the market was maintained. Thereafter, the market fluctuated between tightness and looseness, remaining unstable. The gold market remained firm, leading to hedging activities by Chinese merchants. Despite the large-scale selling by banks, the market was able to hold up. The situation was tight for forward months and slightly closer for swap rates. Finally, Reuters and the Associated Press reported that US banks had sent 46 senators to jointly petition the government to raise the silver price, slightly loosening the trend. At the close, the selling price for sterling was 1 shilling, 7 pence, 635 points, and the US dollar was 40.3125 yuan. Compared to the previous close, sterling was flat, and the spread narrowed by 0.0625. Forward rates were tighter, and swap rates were slightly closer. Chinese merchants bought over 100,000 pounds sterling and over 700,000 yuan US dollars. Cantonese banks also vigorously bought, and Sassoon also bought slightly. George Chih-fu sold. The Central Bank sold forward shillings, and HSBC supplied forward shillings aggressively. Other banks also had strong selling intentions. The transaction record for the half-day is recorded below:

Bank Closing Settlements Push Call Loans to Six Jiao Again 192

Yesterday, the silver market rebounded strongly. With the banks' mid-year closing settlements approaching and relief funds delayed due to procedural issues, general sentiment became nervous, and the demand for funds increased. Although the interbank lending rate remained at two jiao in the morning and afternoon, the call loan rate surged by two jiao, consistently trading at six jiao. In the bill market, over 2.1 million was cleared in the morning session, with over 200,000 in new transactions. There were no transactions in the afternoon session. Transactions in the Small General Association totaled over 600,000. Pledged silver transactions involved over 200,000 in purchases and over 300,000 in new deals. Currency transactions saw over 600,000 withdrawn. On the issuance side, circulating notes amounted to 400,000, secret-mark notes 400,000, remittances from various routes 300,000, customer sources 200,000, and outflows 100,000. Regarding bank settlements, foreign banks settled over 1.8 million in bills, over 2.9 million in various collateralized loans, over 500,000 in special remittances, over 800,000 in foreign exchange settlements, and 400,000 in withdrawals. Chinese banks settled over 2.1 million in bills, over 3.7 million in various collateralized loans, over 600,000 in special remittances, over 1 million in foreign exchange settlements, and 200,000 in deposits. Japanese banks settled over 1.5 million in bills, over 2.7 million in various collateralized loans, over 300,000 in special remittances, over 500,000 in foreign exchange settlements, and 200,000 in deposits. Money shops settled over 2.7 million in silver public orders, over 320,000 in call loan settlements, and cash settlements were consistent. The price of small silver from Jiangnan was 130 yuan in both the morning and afternoon sessions, unchanged from the previous day. The volume of transactions was 3,000 jiao in both the morning and afternoon sessions. The price of small silver from Guangdong remained at 731.8 yuan in the morning session. The volume of transactions was active in the afternoon session, changing to 732.9 yuan, resulting in an increase of 1.1 yuan compared to the previous day. The volume of transactions was 120,000 jiao in the morning session and 140,000 jiao in the afternoon session. Securities: Settlement Nears, Bond Market Suffers Another Setback; Sharp Drop of One Yuan at the Start, Followed by Recovery Due to Arbitrage 193

Yesterday at the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce Securities Exchange, with only the last two days remaining for trading this month, both bulls and bears were heavily involved in rollovers, and the market should have stabilized temporarily. Unexpectedly, groundless rumors suddenly emerged in the market, causing considerable shock at this approaching settlement. Bullish parties dumped their holdings, while retail investors made some new sales, resulting in a sudden drop of over one yuan. Later, due to strong buying by large investors and support from arbitrage trading, the market gradually stabilized, and shares in demand flourished at the close. For the future trend, with only the last day remaining for trading this month, some squeezing is inevitable, but both bulls and bears are generally prepared, and there should be no drastic changes. At the opening yesterday morning, rumors suddenly spread in the market that the 14th issue would be abandoned, causing the price to plummet by half a yuan. After that, due to the absorption by issues 4, 47, the market turned slightly calmer. However, later, due to the rush selling by sellers, the downward trend resumed. Issues 70, 53, and 48 all experienced selling, with the gold shorts suddenly dropping by over one yuan, and the rest uniformly dropping by several jiao. In the second session, leading issues were sluggish by about five fen to four jiao, while the rear issues, particularly 4, 47, turned upward due to strong demand. At the opening of the afternoon session, arbitrage trading became increasingly active, with issues 35, 43, and 46 continuing to be absorbed, and the market price continued to rise by five fen to three jiao. At the close, due to good news in the evening paper, issues 74 and 4 continued to be bought, while issues 11, 53, and 78 also experienced considerable selling. As a result, the market recovered by a few jiao. Overall, the final market price for the day was uniformly down by two or three jiao to five or six jiao, with a total transaction amount of 24,760,000 yuan. Yarn and Cotton: Positive News, Yarn Market Recovers Quickly; Market Sentiment Excited: Price Increases Restrained 195

The soaring situation in the yarn market is unusually strong, due to the emergence of rumors in the market that a certain old matter would be brought up again, and that yarn factories would resume reducing production, causing excitement. Short sellers covered their positions, and bulls added to their positions, with both sides advancing in tandem. As a result, the upward momentum became stronger and stronger. In fact, the market has been falling for a long time, and once it rebounds, it is difficult to stop.

Futures Yarn Soars by Two and a Half Yuan

At the opening of the front market for standard yarn, the situation this month was extremely chaotic. Rumors were rampant in the market, saying that the standard gold had broken through the 800 yuan level. Tat Kee was bidding to buy in this month, calling out 170 yuan. After the bulls spat out some, the market recovered slightly. The opening jump was 2.8 yuan, and the far months followed with a rise of 0.9 jiao. In the second and third sessions, foreign merchants sold short again, and the market quickly reversed. As a result, the near month rose by 1.2 yuan compared to the closing price of the previous day, and the far month rose by 7.8 jiao. At the opening of the afternoon session, the current month was still flat, down by 0.5 jiao. When the market was snapped up to the far month, it suddenly became tight. Discussions were rampant in the market, and all the news was positive. The market price rose step by step, and the market sentiment was extremely sharp. As a result, all months rose by 1.2 yuan to 1.78 yuan compared to the morning closing price. Grains: High Prices Expected, Flour and Wheat Both Rise 198

Yesterday in the flour market, the atmosphere had stabilized in the morning, because imported wheat from Chicago was good by about 1-2 jiao, and Canadian wheat was good by 0.25. Although actual sales were small, factory production also decreased accordingly. The selling of all futures contracts was on hold due to fear of future risks. Demand therefore turned solid leading to market stabilisation. At the opening in the afternoon, both near-term and forward contracts became more expensive. There were rumors about changes in the cargo structure, so some short sellers were eager to cover their positions, and the bulls also took advantage of the situation, with considerable absorption. Due to credit conditions this month, the degree of increase was still slight, and the forward contracts were particularly enthusiastic. Observing the future, both drought and flooding are a concern, and the ups and downs of the market may depend on this. As a result, the current month rose by 1 fen, July rose by 1 fen and 2.5 li, August rose by 1 fen and 1.5 li, September rose by 2 fen, October rose by 1 fen and 1.5 li, and November rose by 2 fen and 7 li.

Yesterday, the wheat market was stable, because quotations for imported wheat were slightly better, and the Saskatchewan Grain Board and the treaty ports were not as enthusiastic as in previous years due to credit conditions. At the opening in the afternoon, the market atmosphere improved, because the flour market rose sharply, and rumors were favorable to rising prices. Metals: Xi'an Traders Purchasing Tinplate 204

Recently, the demand for narrow strip tinplate of one inch or more from local manufacturers in this area has been low, resulting in a quiet market. Over the past few days, shipments of three to four hundred boxes have been sent. Narrow strip tinplate is particularly popular in that city, accounting for about seventy to eighty percent of the purchases. The price is around twenty yuan for narrow strips and twenty-eight yuan for prime tinplate. Additionally, traders from Hankou, Sichuan, and Changsha are also placing substantial orders for narrow strip goods. Although prices haven't increased, the quality and sturdiness are far superior to what they used to be.

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

Ambition 205

— Yi Yi Cottage Owner

Everyone has aspirations; that is, each person has their own "ambition." A's "ambition" cannot be forced upon B, nor can B's "ambition" be forced upon A. For example, A's "ambition" might be in farming, while B's "ambition" is in craftsmanship. If you were to force A, who is inclined to farming, to do craftwork, it would certainly not work. Similarly, forcing B, who is inclined to craftwork, to farm would also be impossible.

Because, one should always pursue endeavors that align with their "ambition" to feel interested. Only by feeling interested can one achieve something. Otherwise, without "ambition," doing things randomly is like a ship without a compass sailing in the ocean! Boundless and without direction, aimlessly drifting about, how easy would it be to reach the destination?

From this perspective, "It is important for a person to have ambition" is indeed not "empty talk." So, dear little friends, where lies your future "ambition"? In farming? In craftsmanship? Or in commerce? Know that the world is vast, and there are more than just these three industries of agriculture, craftsmanship, and commerce. There are many other careers! It all depends on setting your "ambition" and pursuing it!

The Childhood of Kettering 206

— Jun Peng

When you hear the rumbling sound of an engine in the sky, you look up and see an airplane like a dragonfly speeding through the air. I think everyone knows that airplanes were invented in 1905 by the American brothers Orville and Wilbur Wright. But who invented the engine in the airplane? It was Kettering. Perhaps few of the children know about him! Now, let me introduce some of his early history below:

Charles Kettering was born in a small village in New York on May 21, 1876. The village was surrounded by hills, and it was inconvenient to get in and out because one had to go around. When he was young and saw this situation, he thought how convenient and effort-saving it would be to have a bicycle to ride back and forth! So he saved up his money and bought a bicycle. Later, he was not satisfied and wanted to install an engine on the bicycle, which would be ten thousand times faster. Therefore, he looked for books on the principles and structure of engines, studied them carefully, and succeeded after several failures, making it many times faster than ordinary bicycles. But he still worked hard to improve it.

Kettering's good fortune came. - In 1907, the All-American Bicycle Competition was held in Florida, and he went to participate, winning first place, and from then on, the whole of America knew about him. Soon, even greater good fortune came. At this time, Bell, the inventor of the telephone, was the president of the American Aviation Association. He knew that Kettering's engine was incomparably excellent, so he personally visited Kettering and asked him to join the Aviation Association and to make his invention of the engine into a refined airplane. This opportunity enabled the American aviation industry to advance by leaps and bounds and have unlimited progress.

Candle Goldfish 207

— Chen Zhi

Little friends, have you seen goldfish? Their round bodies, bright red scales, protruding eyes, and fluffy tails are so beautiful! If you like them, you can use candle wax to make goldfish that look exactly like the real thing to play with. Here is how to make goldfish:

Mix red and white candle wax to make a goldfish model with a red back and a light red belly. Stick some iron filings on the abdomen, in the right amount, not too much or too little, so that it can remain still in any position in the water. Cover the iron filings with another layer of candle wax so that they cannot be seen. This completes the active goldfish.

When playing, put the goldfish in a glass of water, and then take a magnet and slowly move it up, down, left, and right outside the glass. The goldfish will follow the magnet and sink and float in the glass. At first glance, it looks like a real goldfish.

Little friends, do you find it strange? Why can the goldfish's body stand upright? Why does the goldfish follow the magnet and float up and down? This principle is easy to understand, because the goldfish's abdomen is attached with iron filings, its center of gravity is on the abdomen, and the body can stand upright; and the magnet has the ability to attract iron filings, so when the magnet moves outside the glass, the goldfish swims in the glass.

Little sapling, not very tall, tender branches, delicate leaves, elder brother diligently catches insects, younger sister diligently waters. Grows longer, grows taller, blooms beautiful flowers, bears sweet peaches; look! The whole garden is full of vitality, all thanks to this little sapling. Little friends! You are little saplings, studying hard every day, exercising all the time; the strength of your motherland depends on you little saplings.

Flying Fish and Swimming Birds 210

— Gong Chao

In the ocean, there is a kind of flying fish that can jump out of the sea and fly as far as five hundred feet. Originally, its pectoral fins are particularly long, as long as the wings of a bird. When it jumps out of the water, it spreads its two pectoral fins and flies as fast as a ship.

It is very unfortunate: In the sea, there are gluttonous sharks and dolphins that want to eat it. When it is chased by them, it escapes into the air, but the albatrosses and other birds in the air are opening their greedy mouths. As soon as they see it escape from the water, they desperately chase it. Therefore, it is often escaping for its life in the double attack of two enemies.

This flying fish is a silvery, large-eyed thing.

Just the opposite, in the birds, there are things that cannot fly but can swim, one of which is the penguin. Penguins are produced in the Southern Ocean. Its wings have become fin-shaped, so it can swim in the water. When swimming, it uses these fin-shaped wings to paddle, going up and down in the water. At first glance, it really doesn't know whether it is a fish or a bird. Its head and back are black, its belly is white, and its feet are short.

It often stands upright, as if looking forward to something, so it is called a penguin.

After reading the above two examples, we can understand that animals, in order to adapt to the environment, can slowly transform a part of their body into a more useful shape in order to adapt to survival.

Pencil 211

— Zhen

"Brother, is the black carbon strip in the pencil made of lead?" Xiang'er showed some suspicion, while holding a pencil in his hand.

"You're wrong. We call it a pencil, but it's not actually made of lead. It's made of graphite," Ji'er replied with a smile.

"Since it's made of graphite, why don't we call it a graphite pencil and insist on calling it a pencil?"

"Generally, people think that graphite is very similar to lead, so they call it a pencil, and pencil is easier to call than graphite pencil."

"Brother, how is a pencil made? Can you tell me?"

"Pencil manufacturing (1) Grind graphite into powder, then mix it with clay and water. (2) Press this graphite mixture into a dough, and then pass it through a long tube in a squeezer to make a thin, elongated strip. There are no wooden pieces at that time. (3) The wooden strips for pencils are mostly cypress, because this kind of tree has straight grain, soft texture, and is easy to cut. First cut it into wooden sections, and then use a machine to cut it into small square wooden strips of uniform length. (4) After the wooden strips are cut, a groove is carved on them at the same time. First apply a layer of glue to the graphite, and then embed it one by one into this groove to make it stick firmly. Then put another piece of wood on top to make a square pencil. (5) Put it on a rounding machine to make a long round pencil. (6) Apply paint and rub it to make the appearance beautiful. After dyeing, wait for it to dry, and then put it in the machine to make it the appropriate length. Then engrave the text on the pencil. Brother, look! A pencil must go through such complicated procedures. You must be more economical when you use a pencil next time!"

Number Lineup 212

— Yi De

The younger brother said to the elder sister: "These days, because of the sports meet, our school practices gymnastics every day. Our group gymnastics has been practiced several times, and the lineup is very neat and spectacular."

The elder sister said: "What's so strange about that? I can ask the numbers to line up! If you don't believe me, you call for a pencil and paper."

The younger brother ran away like flying, and ran back with a pencil and paper like flying, and said to the elder sister: "Please tell me quickly, how can the numbers be lined up?"

The elder sister said: "You use thirty-seven to multiply by three, use thirty-seven to multiply by six, to multiply by nine, and the numbers will line up."

The younger brother followed the elder sister's words and multiplied like this

After the younger brother multiplied, he took a look and couldn't help but be happy and said: "Elder sister! What you said is really good, the numbers multiplied out are really lined up in neat lines!"

The elder sister said: "Not only can the three numbers 1, 2, and 3 line up, but the other numbers 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, and 9 can also line up."

The younger brother hurriedly asked the elder sister to tell him, and the elder sister said: "Still use thirty-seven to multiply. You remember: use thirty-seven to multiply by twelve, fifteen, eighteen, twenty-one, twenty-four, twenty-seven. As long as you don't multiply wrong, they will all line up in neat lines."

The younger brother followed the numbers that the elder sister said and multiplied one by one, multiplied out like this:

After the younger brother multiplied and took a look, he couldn't help but clap his hands and said with great joy: "This kind of arithmetic game is really extremely ingenious!"

Hand Care 213

— (Tu Hongxia)

"Hands," everyone has two. There are a few things that these two should pay attention to:

(1) Nails should be trimmed often to avoid hiding dirt.

(2) Wash hands before eating to avoid germs following food into the stomach and causing illness.

(3) Wash hands after eating to avoid the greasy food staining hands and clothes.

(4) Fingers should not be put in the mouth.

(5) Do not scratch the skin arbitrarily, as it can cause skin diseases.

(6) Dirty things should not come into contact with hands.

(7) Wash hands often with medicated soap.

(8) If a knife punctures a finger, disinfect and stop the bleeding quickly.

Little friends! Above are eight points regarding hand care. I hope everyone will keep them in mind at all times.

A Small Record of the Founding Conference of the Chinese Children's Culture Association 214

— Chao Yi

The Chinese Children's Culture Association, which had been in preparation for a long time, held its founding conference on the sixteenth. The meeting place was on the third floor of the Continental Department Store on Nanjing Road. It was arranged very neatly and elegantly. Many people attended, including several children. I looked at everyone's smiling faces and the place where the association was born, and I felt unspeakable joy in my heart.

At the beginning of the meeting, Mr. Huang Jiping, a reporter from this newspaper, presided. He said that this association was established to build a beautiful cultural landscape for our country's children and to seek happiness for the children. He showed a kind of enthusiastic emotion when he spoke. Then, Mr. Lin Yin reported on the work of the preparatory period: holding literacy service groups with little teachers, broadcasting children's music, etc. At this time, I suddenly remembered the "New Children's Song" a few days ago, and the singing seemed to still be in my ears.

Originally, there were also speeches by Mr. Pan Gongzhan and Tao Zhixing, but they could not come because of something. Later, the charter was discussed. Many proposals were also passed: holding children's book and newspaper exhibitions regularly, organizing children's libraries, setting up children's book and newspaper cars, ... I hope everyone will implement them quickly.

In addition, I heard that there are news of various places asking to organize branches. In the future, I really want to ask my younger brother and younger sister to join the association nearby and do this great work together.

When the meeting adjourned, the lights all around were on. I went home in the light. Although I walked a long way, I didn't feel tired at all.

Remarks on "Fishing in the Sea" 215

— Fisherman of Wusong Fisheries School

On May 10th, I read an article titled "Fishing in the Sea" in the Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly. The author's dissemination of fisheries knowledge to children is certainly worthy of our admiration, but the objects depicted in the illustration accompanying that article are somewhat different from the real thing. From what I know, I will correct it a little bit, which may be welcome by the original author who advocates fisheries education?

In the original picture, we saw a fishing vessel towing a net forward, and another net stretched out in the sea. Both of these things have errors.

First, let's talk about the error of the fishing vessel towing the net: There are two types of fishing vessels towing nets, namely: trawl fishing vessels and double-trawl fishing vessels. The former uses one vessel to tow one net, and the latter uses two vessels to tow one net (the structure of the vessels and nets is of course different). The original picture is a trawl fishing vessel, but there are some errors in the towing cable and the net: there are two towing cables, each with a length of one hundred and twenty fathoms, and a diameter of one inch, twisted from six strands of net silk rope. One end of the towing net is tied to the towing cable car on the deck (divided into left and right towing cable cars), and the other end is tied to the net board at the mouth of the net. When fishing begins, the net is locked to the east lock of the towing cable. From the angle formed by the two nets, the size of the opening of the turning net can be known, so if you want the opening of the net to be large, just enlarge the angle, and if you want the opening of the net to be small, just reduce the angle formed by the cable! The operating time of the vessel towing the net is about three hours each time, and usually only six or seven catches can be made in one day and night; each voyage out to sea for fishing takes about ten days.

Second, let's talk about the net stretched out in the sea. That kind of net is the so-called gill net, and the net for catching anchovies (those with eggs are called kaozi fish) is also one of them. In addition to the net body and floats, there are sinkers and float tubes on the net. Because of the floats and sinkers, the net body is floated upwards by the floats, and sunk downwards by the sinkers, so that the net is opened up and down. In addition, a float tube is tied to one end of the net, and most of the fishing vessels are sailing vessels.

The above is just a correction of the errors in the original picture. However, the little friends may not understand, so I think it would be best to ask your teachers to lead you to visit the fishing vessels, fishing boats, fisheries experiment fields, or fisheries schools, then the knowledge you see and hear in the book and on paper will be more accurate and more!

The Adventures of Sinbad the Sailor (23) 216

— Xin Qing

Sinbad's Last Voyage

At the end of this sixth voyage, I returned home, and I resolved to spend the rest of my life in my hometown.

One day, I was hosting a banquet for some friends when a servant came to inform me that a merchant from the court wanted to speak to me. I got up and went out to see him.

"The king sent me to say that he must speak to you," he said.

Naturally, I had to leave my guests and go to court immediately. I was led into the king's chamber, I kissed the ground before him, and he spoke to me.

He said: "Ah! Sinbad, I have something for you to do. I want you to send a letter and a gift to the King of Serendib."

I said, "Your Majesty, I have sworn never to leave my home in Baghdad again. If you can find someone who is worthy of doing this for you, I will be happy; if you cannot find anyone, then I am here to obey your command."
