Women's World

A Review of the Chinese Women's Movement 217

— Luo Qiong

Also Discussing Mr. Wang Jiaoying's "Letter to Editor Shi Yin of 'Women and Youth'"

Mr. Wang Xiaoying published a letter in the 68th issue of this journal, "Letter to Editor Shi Yin of 'Women and Youth,'" discussing the reasons for and significance of the Chinese women's movement. In the current "smog-filled" stage of the Chinese women's movement, a re-evaluation of this issue is indeed very necessary. In addition to admiring Mr. Wang's attention to the women's movement, I dare not hide my own views. I intend to follow Mr. Wang's lead, adhering to the instruction that "we women seem to have a responsibility to pay attention to this letter," and humbly offer my ignorant opinions for Mr. Wang's consideration:

(1) An Analysis of the Current Stage of the Chinese Women's Movement:

In the current stage of the Chinese women's movement, the most common prevailing arguments are roughly the following two:

(A) Abolish the women's movement. Here, there are three different opinions circulating. First, as Mr. Shi Yin says:

"Men and women cannot be independent and separate. Why should 'women's movement' become a separate term, as if it has its own independent cause? It is very obvious that we regard it as natural and not strange for women to have 'women's associations,' but if men also have 'men's associations,' wouldn't it be ridiculous? I think this is the fundamental mistake of the so-called 'women's movement,' to divide men and women into two classes to confront each other. As for the 'women's rights movement,' the word 'rights' leads people to struggle, so naturally it is even more unworthy" (Women and Youth, issue 141).

This opinion is not due to "misunderstandings" arising from the current "Chinese 'women's movement' being incomplete or nominal," but is clearly a distortion produced by Mr. Shi Yin's insufficient understanding of social issues, or even his deliberate obfuscation of social issues. Undeniably, in the current society, men and women have common ground in their status. At the same time, everyone will admit that although women have already obtained the empty principle of "equality between men and women," in reality, whether in politics, society, or economics, the inequality of status between men and women still exists. Here, of course, we cannot "divide men and women into two classes to confront each other," but as long as the specific fact of "inequality" exists, Mr. Shi Yin cannot dissolve the specific into the general and deny the necessity of the women's movement. As for whether the "women's movement" should adopt the "women's rights movement" approach, I will discuss it in the next section.

The second opinion believes that since the women's movement was loudly advocated from the May Fourth Movement until now, the result has only been to add "campus belles" to schools and "vases" to institutions, and believes that this result is entirely the product of the women's movement, and so it recklessly shouts for the abolition of the women's movement. If this attempt is not deliberately intended to make "women forever subordinate to men," it is simply a case of "throwing the baby out with the bathwater." I believe that the reason why the women's movement has achieved such results is not in the women's movement itself, but in the failure to adequately solve the entire social problem. This fact does not prove that the women's movement cannot exist, but only proves that the women's problem cannot be solved separately from the entire social problem. In this light, the reason why the women's liberation of the current stage has degenerated and become corrupt is entirely the result of seeking a way out under the current situation. Therefore, if the previous proposition uses the general to obliterate the specific, then this proposition wants to use the specific to obliterate the general itself: when the specific itself cannot solve the problem, even the specific itself is obliterated.

The third opinion is even more "straightforward and blunt," and does not, like the previous two, hide under some kind of mask to complete its attempt to "send women home"; instead, it openly brandishes the banner of "virtuous wife and good mother," ordering "women to go home," or using "pleasant" words like "the solution to the women's problem lies in obtaining family happiness. If one can understand moral responsibility, understand tolerance, patience, and calmness in the family, one will naturally obtain happiness," to anesthetize women, making them "willingly serve" as domestic slaves. People of this kind superficially hang up the sign of the women's movement, but their abolition of the women's movement and betrayal of women's interests is already obvious to all and needs no further criticism; the above three propositions, whether directly or indirectly abolishing the women's movement, are all using restorationist methods to anesthetize the progressive consciousness of young women, all attempting to sacrifice women to temporarily alleviate the current economic and political crisis.

(B) Acknowledging that the women's movement has a necessity to exist, while at the same time believing that the current stage of the Chinese women's movement is still stagnating in the "women's rights movement" stage. Mr. Wang is a staunch advocate of this view. In her letter to Mr. Shi Yin, she said, "You say that the 'women's rights movement' leads people to struggle with the word 'rights,' which is not right. This sounds right on the surface; but now that men are depriving women of their rights and freedoms, we should not embrace a non-resistance doctrine and make women succumb to the iron hooves of men and allow them to be slaughtered." From these few words, it is clear that Mr. Wang is embracing "Nora's courage," from the May Fourth Movement to the present, sticking to a consistent position, and stubbornly wanting to thoroughly complete the principle of "equality" between men and women. Her spirit of struggle is certainly admirable; however, she has isolated the women's movement from the entire social problem, failing to see the historical background of the women's rights movement; as a result, the due development of the Chinese women's movement has also been neglected, and the result is that she will forever embrace the women's rights movement of the "May Fourth era," growing old together, and unknowingly becoming a sacrifice of the times.

(2) The Social Background of the Women's Movement

Based on the above analysis, there is no need to elaborate on the various opinions on abolishing the women's movement. However, it is necessary to conduct a detailed review of the women's rights movement to determine its significance. In order to understand this issue more clearly, I intend to describe it in three points: 1. The occurrence of the women's movement, 2. The temporality of the women's rights movement, 3. The women's problem in capitalist society.

According to Mr. Wang's opinion, the occurrence of the women's movement, which is also the reason for its existence, is because "men... have become a special class" to women, and the purpose of the women's movement is "to awaken women's own consciousness and resist all the oppression given by men, to eliminate the class between the sexes and create a world of absolute equality between men and women." This abstract concept, just as Mr. Wang said, "seems to be very right on the surface," but once you look at the reality, it feels as if it is right and wrong. The emergence of all social problems has a certain economic structure as its basis; at the same time, the solution to all social problems must also be at a certain stage of economic development, that is, within the limits allowed by economic development, before it is possible. In history, since the collapse of the golden age of equality between men and women – the primitive communal society – women were not allowed to participate in social productive labor and were restricted within the family. Men, relying on their private property rights, forced women to be subordinate to their authority. Therefore, women cannot be equal to men in politics, economics, and society. This situation reached its peak in the feudal era. If we follow Mr. Wang's argument, at this time, women must rise up to "resist all the oppression given by men." But this is not the case; at that time, there was clearly no women's movement. What existed was only deceptive etiquette such as "three obediences and four virtues." No one can deny that the women's movement is a special product of capitalist development. Why did the women's movement only emerge at this time? Perhaps some people believe it is because at this time, there were "pioneers" who rose up to "awaken women's own consciousness." Even if this is correct, we still have to ask why these "pioneers" were not born in slave society and feudal society, but only in capitalist society? Or why would they be treated as rebels and severely punished in slave society and feudal society, but praised in capitalist society, and even be able to join the ranks of men and "hold official positions," etc.?

Originally, after the Industrial Revolution, with the large-scale development of capitalism, the need for free laborers became more and more urgent. First, the shackles of the majority of men selling their labor were eliminated through "serf emancipation." Furthermore, as capitalism continued to develop, the prisoners who had been imprisoned in their homes for thousands of years – women – had to be expelled from their families and dragged into factories in large numbers. The progress of the division of labor and the adoption of machines gradually made it possible for women's labor to be widely adopted; at the same time, the low wages of female workers catered to the greed of factory owners even more. However, the heavy shackles of feudal morality hindered the progress of the "women leaving home" movement; the women's problem was thus a product of this contradiction, and the women's movement gained its conditions for existence to solve this contradiction.

For example, the women's movement during the French Revolution was because, from the 15th to the 18th centuries, the strict regulations of the guilds confined the field of women's occupations to a very narrow space, and the field of productive activity was completely occupied by men. Thus, working women demanded "equal rights with men in labor," which, in other words, was "absolute freedom of labor." They also knew very clearly that "to have freedom of labor, it is essential to abolish the feudal system and destroy the guild organizations." In order to achieve this goal, they also enthusiastically participated in the bourgeois democratic revolution of the time, under the banner of freedom and equality.

With the development of capitalism, the women's rights movement in various countries has successively achieved more or less success; the principle of equality between men and women has at least been recognized in theory. However, although the women's rights movement has achieved considerable success, the women's problem has clearly not been thoroughly solved. Because women have broken away from feudal bondage, they are also bound by capital. After their liberation, they still cannot become healthy women in the ideal sense, and are even forced to become "vases," "dance stars," etc. The political power that can be obtained in capitalist society is originally only established to protect the interests of special positions; therefore, the rights obtained by women in the women's rights movement naturally cannot exceed the general level. Moreover, due to various traditional relationships (mainly property rights, etc., which are generally still monopolized by men), women are generally more backward than men in politics, economics, and culture; their scope of work is far narrower than that of men, and the treatment they receive is also not as good as that of men. Therefore, in capitalist society, women on the one hand partially break away from the shackles of the family and participate in social production work, and are exploited by capitalists; on the other hand, they are also more or less affected by the remnants of feudalism and are still trapped under the control of men. The women's problem of the current stage has emerged from these two layers of shackles. Therefore, the solution to this problem is of course not something that the anti-feudal women's rights movement of the previous stage can accomplish. Only by linking it to the entire social relationship that gives rise to the women's problem can we obtain the key to thoroughly solving the women's problem of the current stage.

(3) China's Social Changes and the Women's Problem

Now that the historical development of the women's movement, especially the temporality of the women's rights movement, is clear, we will now observe the core of the Chinese women's problem at the current stage and its solution. In order to correctly understand this point, we must first analyze China's social changes before addressing the problem itself.

Since the Opium War, the sprouts of capitalism have begun to grow in China, and the women's liberation movement that closely followed has also gradually begun to emerge. During World War I, the economic aggression of the great powers temporarily eased, and China's national industry developed rapidly. At this time, the demands of the emerging bourgeoisie to resist feudal forces and even lift the economic shackles of the great powers became increasingly strong; at the same time, the idea of equality between men and women also permeated the country. The vigorous May Fourth Movement was the product of this social change. Following the considerable success of the May Fourth Movement, especially the subsequent May 30th Incident and the National Revolution of 1926-27, the restrictions on women in education, occupation, and marriage were gradually opened, and women's participation in politics and inheritance rights were also recognized by law. The Chinese women's rights movement came to an end at this point.

Naturally, the Chinese women's rights movement not only cannot exceed the general achievements of various countries, but is even below the general level. Because China is a semi-colonial country: the economic aggression of the great powers makes the development of China's national capital particularly difficult, so its anti-feudal task cannot be thoroughly completed. Correspondingly, the feudal shackles suffered by Chinese women are actually far greater than those of Britain, the United States, and other countries. On the other hand, under the control of this foreign capital, it is extremely difficult for Chinese national capital to develop. Therefore, they have to use more backward and more harmful methods to deal with working women. Mr. Wang said, "Now the center of Chinese politics is men, the center of society is men," and what about the center of the family? At the same time, she pointed out various facts of inequality in politics, economics, and society. These are certainly correct; however, we can no longer simply attribute these phenomena to the fact that the women's rights movement has not been successful, and it certainly cannot be solved by the women's rights movement. The "vases and dance stars" that I mentioned before, especially the various inhuman lives endured by factory women and rural women in this bleak and dilapidated countryside, cannot be solved by the right to participate in politics, "the right to inherit, and all kinds of 'freedom and equality' slogans." It is as clear as fire that the women's rights movement cannot solve the current stage of China's women's problem.

In summary, we know that the Chinese women's problem, like those of other countries, is based on general social problems, and at the same time, in this general context, the women's problem has its own special significance and can still become an independent women's liberation movement. However, since the women's problem is based on the entire social problem, then the women's problem naturally cannot be solved separately from the entire social problem. In this era of the decline of world capitalism, especially in this semi-colonial China, wanting to rely solely on the women's rights movement "based on the principle of (men and women) equality, to jointly develop their knowledge and abilities and create a beautiful and free family and society" is probably just a surreal fantasy. Mr. Wang is not satisfied with personal achievements and still loudly cries out "weeping for the two hundred million pitiful women." This spirit is most admirable; however, at this time, to promote a narrow women's rights movement, even if it is not intentionally concealing more important social contradictions, I am afraid it will still be in vain. As the old saying goes, "Even a fool has something to offer in a thousand thoughts." I wonder if Mr. Wang is willing to accept this "foolish opinion," which may be called a "gain"?

After Reading "Letter to Editor Shi Yin of 'Women and Youth'" 218

— Gao Hongshou

In a letter "To Editor Shi Yin of 'Women and Youth'" (see Shen Bao's Women's Corner, June 9th), Xiao Yin-jun (Mr. Wang Jiaoying) argued against Shi Yin-jun's statement, "The term 'women's rights movement' stirs up strife and is therefore not worth pursuing," saying, "Now that men are depriving women of their rights and freedoms, should we simply remain passive and allow 400 million women to be trampled under men's iron hooves?" She sees that men are at the center of politics, society, and family in China, but her view is narrow.

Considering the family unit—a husband and wife—created by two sexes, either the husband or wife could claim the family is his or her own. However, often, the husband alone works outside the home and provides for the family (exceptions exist). Thus, the husband is at the center of the family. This is based on the reality, not that men are occupying all the centers. It is women who are incapable and give up their role. This is true not only in China but in other countries as well.

We all know the saying: "The capable are employed, and the wise advise; those who labor with their hands are ruled by others, and those who labor with their minds rule." Unless there are differences in knowledge that create social hierarchies, no one can dominate another. Therefore, I disagree with Xiao Yin-jun's statement: "Men have become a special class toward women. The women's movement seeks to eliminate class between men and women. Men are in a dominant position, and their authority over women has reached its peak."

Xiao Yin-jun need not cite examples from the Family Law in the Civil Code, such as "After marriage, a woman should take her husband's surname and residence. Children should take their father's surname…" as strong evidence—as if she is her husband's possession, managing his household, and raising his children—that women's activities are controlled by men, and her life is like that of a domesticated animal in a farming family. In fact, the wife takes her husband's surname because the husband is more likely to represent the family and interact with the outside world, unifying the family's identity. The husband's residence is the family he and his wife created together, so the wife is living in her own home. There is no need to argue about these two points.

The children also take the father's surname, which is simply a consequence of the wife taking her husband's surname. However, even if children could take the mother's surname, men and women would still not be absolutely equal. Therefore, it is best to combine both parents' surnames. If this were implemented, the grandchildren would have four-character surnames. As for raising children, due to the husband's biological limitations, it is naturally the wife's responsibility. However, it should be clear that the children are the creation of both husband and wife, and the wife is not raising the husband's children alone. In short, everything is a voluntary obligation undertaken by the husband and wife in the spirit of mutual assistance, using their respective strengths. There is no reason for the husband to dominate the wife and make her work like an animal.

In terms of economics, Xiao Yin-jun also sees the Civil Code's statement that "Profits from a wife's property belong to the husband, who has the right to use her property…" as evidence of male economic aggression. Men are indeed excessive in this respect. I hope this can be corrected to prevent a husband's bankruptcy from causing the wife to go bankrupt as well. However, most women still do not engage in productive work and have no source of income. To fight over property inherited from parents or in-laws is ugly.

Xiao Yin-jun also says, "Besides political and economic aggression, men also use cultural aggression, such as advocating the education of 'virtuous women and good mothers'…" But if a wife is not virtuous and a mother is not good, how can they achieve gender equality and create a happy family? Therefore, this is not an aggressive policy by men. Instead, men should be questioned for not allowing women to act independently, and there should be an advocacy for the education of "virtuous husbands and good fathers." There is no aggression to speak of. Based on these reasons, women still have the potential to struggle. Unfortunately, most do not struggle or struggle in the wrong direction.

In conclusion, after reading Xiao Yin-jun's article, I believe she is relatively optimistic. However, I hope she will encourage women to engage in productive work and establish a better position for women, instead of engaging in superficial disputes about women's rights.

Shen Bao Local Supplement: Amateur Weekly

Amateur Idle Talk

"Small Farmer Cooperative Production" to Save the Rural Villages 221

— Guo Jing

Eighty percent of the country's farmers are the lifeblood of our nation, and the one million rural villages across the country are its soul. However, examining the so-called lifeblood of our nation today, it truly only has its last breath remaining. And the so-called soul of our nation is already tending towards the dangerous path of death and extinction. The bankruptcy of rural villages has been shouted about with earth-shaking clamor, but to this day, there is still not a truly effective method to rescue the people from fire and water, or offer some benefit in reality.

The root causes of the difficult lives of farmers today are indeed extraordinarily complex. Such as the uneven distribution of land, the defects of the social system, and the extension of the giant claws of imperialist economic forces, all of which are contributing factors. However, the backwardness of agricultural production technology is the biggest factor contributing to farmers' lives nearing the brink of death. Therefore, instead of loudly singing about saving the country and merely creating empty promises, it would be better to start with improving production technology and increasing production efficiency, finding a path to survival for the wounded farmers, and allowing the collapsing rural villages to see a road of light. This would be a more sensible approach.

So, how can we improve production technology? How can we increase production efficiency? I believe the best method is "small farmer cooperative production."

Farmers have always been limited by the confines of their knowledge, their conservative inertia, and their self-interested selfishness, coupled with a lack of guidance and assistance. Therefore, farmers only adhere to old methods and do not know what new production techniques are, and naturally, they do not know the convenience, economy, and effectiveness of cooperative production. The result of them operating their own farms separately is that they not only waste labor and money, but also end up with a painful outcome of being unable to maintain their livelihoods.

Someone investigated the income of an average farmer's family in a certain county in Jiangnan:

They cultivate ten mu of land. The summer rice crop yields an average of one and a half shi per mu, averaging eight yuan per shi, totaling one hundred and twenty yuan. The winter wheat crop yields an average of eight dou per mu, averaging six yuan per shi, totaling forty-eight yuan. Rice and wheat stalks yield two yuan, totaling one hundred and seventy yuan in income. Subtracting three yuan per mu for fertilizer, the actual income after offsetting expenses is one hundred and forty yuan. An additional fifty-four yuan is earned from vegetables, livestock, and silkworm rearing, and forty yuan from other side occupations. The total annual income is two hundred and thirty-four yuan.

Furthermore, according to Mr. Gu Fu's statistics, the annual living expenses for a family of five, including the elderly and young, are:

(1) Food expenses: rice and wheat cost thirty cents per day, nine yuan per month, and one hundred and eight yuan per year; vegetables and meat cost ten cents per day, thirty-six yuan per year; firewood, charcoal, salt, and soy sauce cost thirty-six yuan per year; (2) Clothing expenses: four yuan per person per year, totaling twenty yuan; (3) House repairs or rent cost twelve yuan per year; (4) Education expenses cost six yuan per year; (5) Socializing with relatives and friends for weddings and funerals costs ten yuan per year; (6) Medical expenses cost ten yuan per year; (7) Funeral expenses cost ten yuan (averaging one hundred yuan every ten years, amortized to ten yuan per year); (8) Taxes cost six yuan; (9) Miscellaneous expenses cost twenty yuan. The total annual expenditure is two hundred and seventy-four yuan.

According to the above statistics, such a farmer's family still has at least forty yuan missing each year. Moreover, we must recognize that this refers to places with fertile land, and years with average harvests. If the soil is barren, or if they encounter floods, droughts, or insect plagues, then their livelihoods are even more unimaginable.

Therefore, if we want to relieve the suffering of farmers and seek the prosperity of the entire nation, we must quickly plan effective methods to increase production, and quickly work together under the banner of cooperative production.

As the saying goes, "Many hands make light work, a single hand cannot clap," and "United will stands like a fortress, a single force cannot prevail." This is true for everything, but especially for agriculture. In the past, Chinese farmers, because they operated agriculture individually, had to provide all agricultural tools themselves. Therefore, if they wanted to adopt new agricultural machinery, individual farmers lacked the capital and were unable to do so, and thus the production effect was reduced. For example, during the severe drought in Jiangnan the year before last, the small rivers dried up, and because they could not jointly organize water pumping, they could only sit and wait for the rice fields to become withered. This is like a sick person who cannot afford to hire a doctor for treatment, and ultimately loses their life. How pitiful and lamentable is this! Normally, most farmers can only treat the immediate symptoms and do not think about improving old-fashioned agricultural tools. Therefore, whenever the weather is relatively dry, they rely entirely on manual or animal power to turn water scoops. Farmers often spend the entire summer wasting away from the labor of scooping water. As a result, the cost is high, but the effectiveness is limited, and in the event of a major drought, the effect is almost zero!

I dare to solemnly shout to the people of the country: If we want to save the suffering of farmers' lives and stabilize the foundation of the nation, we should unanimously advocate that all old methods of individual cultivation should be abolished as soon as possible, and that we should unite and move towards the new path of "cooperative production." Only cooperative production can destroy Asian-style production technology, and only cooperative production can utilize scientific production methods.

Overseas Correspondence Network

The Soon-to-be-Completed Singapore Naval Base 222

— Hua Mei

Malaya Peninsula Correspondence

Singapore is a small island in the southern part of the Malaya Peninsula. Five hundred years ago, it was still a desolate fishing village. However, since the invasion of European powers, in the last century, this desolate fishing village has transformed into the world's ninth-largest port. Now, Britain is working hard to build the Singapore naval base, strengthening Singapore's naval base, which is expected to be completed within this year. According to British military journalists, after completion, the Singapore naval base will be the fourth most excellent combat base in the world.

As early as 1919, Admiral Jellicoe, after inspecting the Far East, suggested that the British government build the Singapore naval

Page 20

base. In April 1923, the Conservative cabinet formally decided to begin construction. However, in 1924, when MacDonald's Labour cabinet was formed, the implementation plan for building the Singapore naval base was suspended on the grounds of arms reduction and peace in the Far East. When the Conservative Party returned to power in 1925, the proposal to build the Singapore naval base was revived. However, the time when active construction began was after 1932, or more specifically, after the Japan's seizing of Northeast China incident.

The British initially budgeted 11 million pounds for the construction of the Singapore naval base, which was later reduced to 7.75 million pounds, but last year's budget increased to 8.93 million pounds. The location of this base is very deep, with no wind or waves, and can accommodate a large number of giant ships. At the same time, there are large-scale naval and air force airfields, planned to accommodate at least 1,000 aircraft. In recent years, Britain has spent a lot of money here to complete breakwaters, radio stations, floating docks, oil storage tanks, and large-scale land fortresses. Now, this huge construction project is actively underway. The original number of workers employed was only 5,000, but has now increased to 14,500. Among them, there are 8,000 Chinese, 4,000 Malays, and 2,000 Indians. For the sake of "military secrecy," the fortress and naval base areas are prohibited from being observed, so all we can see here are groups of workers transporting materials such as iron bars and steel columns, many "Royal Air Force" planes flying in the sky from time to time, the actions of the British Empire's army, navy, and air force, and searchlights shining all night long.

Singapore is the center of the Europe-Asia shipping route and the hub of the South Seas islands. It is 6,000 nautical miles from the British main fleet's base at Moorshead, and only 1,600 nautical miles from Japan's Sasebo. If the distance between Singapore and Sasebo or Nagasaki is compared with the distance from Pearl Harbor to Yokohama (3,400 nautical miles), the former is much closer. Therefore, from Japan's perspective, Britain's construction of the Singapore naval base is not only to defend its territories in the Pacific and Indian Oceans, but also to threaten Sasebo, Taiwan, and Japan. In fact, in recent years, due to the active development of Japanese power towards China and the South Seas, Britain has indeed felt greatly uneasy. The active construction of the Singapore naval base is indeed an attempt to maintain its hegemony in the Far East, and also to defend against Japan. The fact that this construction project only began to be actively implemented after the Northeast China Incident shows the intentions of the British Empire. Recently, it has been heard that Tokyo has plans to lend money to the Siamese government to build a canal across the Kra Isthmus in Siam. If this canal is completed, not only will all of Singapore's commercial value be taken away, but the military value of the Singapore naval base will also be reduced. Conservative members of the British House of Commons have made the following remarks about this matter: "The plan for Siam to build a canal is worthy of discussion, as it is said to be built with funds borrowed from Japan. If this plan is realized, it will have a great impact on our military fortress in the Malay Peninsula. We must not forget the opening of the Panama Canal, which has great naval and military importance in the Western Hemisphere." From this, we can not only see the importance the British attach to their "military fortress in the Malay Peninsula," but also the conflict between Britain and Japan in the Far East.

Recently, Japan has been very active in Singapore, and Britain's defenses have also been tightened. Therefore, although it seems "quiet" on the surface, in reality it is as if the Pacific War has already broken out, and the atmosphere is very tense.

Singapore has four to five hundred thousand residents, two-thirds of whom are Chinese. However, these Chinese compatriots, under the rule of the British Empire, have not only failed to pay attention to the national crisis in their motherland, but even cannot speak Chinese! The languages they use are English and Malay dialects. If you do not understand English and Malay dialects, when you come to Singapore, you will not be able to talk to the Chinese compatriots here.

Celebrity Interview Record

The King of Flour 223

— Shen Qianli

It was a sunny afternoon when I met Mr. Rong Zongjing in his writing room. A short old man with an unremarkable appearance and plain clothes was sitting at a large desk. Anyone who walked in would not believe that this was the "King of Flour" who owned nine yarn factories and eight flour mills. No wonder I asked, "Is Mr. Rong Zongjing here?" after seeing him in person.

As I walked into this simply furnished writing room, Mr. Rong stood up and walked towards me to greet me.

"What can I do for you?" he asked with a cheerful smile on his face.

"I've come especially to visit you and to learn about the process of how you started your business."

"Ah!" he smiled again, saying in his thick Wuxi accent, "My surname is Rong!"

"Oh... I'm very sorry. Because I've never met you before, I didn't recognize you in person." I felt small, and my face was hot, as if I had eaten chili peppers.

"Please sit down!" he said, pressing a doorbell on the wall. After a while, a servant brought in two cups of tea, and he exchanged courtesies with me for a while.

"You don't need to be so polite," I said, slightly shifting my body. "Mr. Rong, do you come here to work every day?"

"I come every day. I'm the same as them (referring to the staff). I come to the writing room at nine o'clock in the morning and two o'clock in the afternoon, and I don't go back for meals until twelve o'clock in the morning and six o'clock in the afternoon."

"That's very hard work," I said.

"It doesn't feel like it. I've been doing this for decades, and now it's become a habit. I'd rather be here than idle at home all day."

"Of course, doing such a big business requires a hardworking spirit. Mr. Rong, do you have to inspect the factories in Shanghai every day?"

"No, because there are people in charge on the side, so I don't necessarily have to go every day, and I wouldn't have enough time. I have more than a dozen yarn factories and flour mills in Shanghai. If I had to inspect each factory once, it would take a whole day." He couldn't help but laugh proudly.

"Mr. Rong, you run so many yarn factories, how is it that you are famous for flour?" I asked curiously.

"There's a reason for that. I thank them for calling me the King of Flour." He took a sip of tea and continued, "It's a long story. I used to run a small business in Wuxi, but I still made some money every year. However, I always felt that this kind of business, although profitable, was not directly beneficial to the people's livelihood. Later, when I came to Shanghai, I saw that a large number of foreign goods were being imported, especially yarn, cloth, and flour, which are related to people's clothing and food. Looking back at the country, no one was paying attention to this industry, so I pooled together several tens of thousands of yuan in capital and started the Fuxin Flour Company. At first, I only opened one factory. Of course! At that time, the scale was very rudimentary, and there was no question of competing with foreign goods, but at least I had recovered a little bit of the leakage in the import surplus of foreign goods. After the first Fuxin factory opened, there was still some money to be earned every year, so I relied on this surplus profit to expand from one factory to two, three, and four factories. Soon, the European War broke out, and the light and heavy industries of various countries were affected by the war and declared closure one after another. The import of foreign goods was not as much as before. Especially flour and cloth. Because they had to supply military needs at that time, later not only was there no surplus to transport to China, but they even had to buy from China. In the four years of the European War, Fuxin sold as many as nine million bags of flour. At that time, the price of each bag of flour was only one yuan higher than that sold in the country. Of course, thanks to the European War, Fuxin earned several million yuan, and my title of "King of Flour" became famous from then on. But at that time, the domestic production of cloth was not enough to supply the demand, and there were not many foreign goods coming in, so the price of cloth became more and more expensive, and the general civilians who could not afford silk were directly affected by this. In this year, I proposed to open the Shenxin Yarn Factory, hoping to solve the current difficult problem from this aspect. Things went very smoothly, and seven yarn factories were established in the first year. But in the second year, because all the funds were concentrated in the yarn factories, there was a period when there was a lack of cash flow, and the debt was several million. The general onlookers were very worried about me at this time, fearing that the future of my business would encounter insurmountable dangers. I myself was very clear about this situation, but I was not flustered at all. In this year, I just buried my head in hard work to cope with the current difficult environment. Sure enough, in the second year's final settlement period, I unexpectedly earned several million yuan, and after paying off all the debts, the working capital also increased. At this time, the British-owned Sanxin Yarn Factory was selling, and I spent several million yuan to take it over. The current Shenxin No. 9 Factory is the reincarnation of the former Sanxin Yarn Factory. However, after I took it over, I spent more than 2.4 million yuan to rebuild all the factory buildings and workers' residences." He said, taking a sip of tea and lightly smacking his lips, as if there was still a lot of aftertaste.

I became more and more interested as I listened, as if listening to a story, and said with a smile, "Mr. Rong is not only the 'King of Flour,' but also a leader in the yarn industry!"

"I wouldn't dare to say that," he shook his head and said, "but I always want to do more businesses that are directly related to the people. Like cloth and flour, I am very interested in them. If there is an opportunity in the future, I may do one or two more industries that are more beneficial to the people's livelihood."

"Mr. Rong, you have such a large fortune now, so your personal life must be..."

"My personal life?" He laughed before I could finish my sentence. "Except for having a car more than ordinary people, everything else is the same as everyone else. Look, almost everything I wear is produced by my own factory. It can be said that I haven't bought a foot of cloth from a cloth shop in the past few years. As for buying odds and ends, the family takes care of it. I myself don't even spend ten yuan a year."

"I heard that you have several young masters, who have probably also been influenced by Mr. Rong and live a very simple life, right?"

"There are three children in total. Two of them are still in charge of some things, and the youngest is studying. My brothers don't mess around. I don't want my children to act like young masters, because China currently needs people who can work hard. When I first started Fuxin Factory, I don't know how many difficulties I encountered, but I have never failed to deal with them calmly. And if a business does not experience these several failures, people will take it very ordinary and will not put in the effort to do it."

Current Affairs Research

The Decline of French Democracy 224

— Zhang Pu

France is the nation where the democratic revolution was most thorough and the birthplace of modern democracy. Therefore, France has always respected "human rights" and "freedom." After the Great War, France further leveraged the control power of the Treaty of Versailles. Internally, it benefited from substantial reparations and other advantages, leading to relatively stable national economy and finances. Externally, the effectiveness of the Versailles system and the role of the League of Nations allowed it to dominate Europe. Thus, while crises arose in Germany, Austria, and other countries after the war, France's political situation remained relatively stable, and the so-called tendency towards extreme politics did not yet emerge. However, good times do not last forever. Since the global economic panic of 1929, the prosperity of capitalist France has been swept away by this wave of panic. As a result, phenomena such as overproduction, trade decline, increased unemployment, rural panic, credit depression, bank closures, and financial crises have increasingly occurred and developed in France. At the same time, France often encountered setbacks in diplomacy. It is evident that Britain, unwilling to see France dominate Europe after the war, frequently created difficulties for it in various aspects. For example, it secretly supported Germany's rearmament and openly advocated for naval equality between France and Italy. Its opposition to Briand's Danube Union plan is a clear illustration. After Hitler came to power, the Versailles system was further destroyed, making France's hegemony even more precarious. Considering France's relations with other European countries, Poland, once its best ally, has seen its foreign policy in Warsaw completely diverge from Paris's intentions in recent years. Germany and Poland have formed an alliance and are aligned in many areas. Similarly, Austria-Hungary was also a country closest to France, but as the conflict between France and Germany intensified, France had to turn a blind eye to Italy's growing influence in Central Europe, drawing Austria-Hungary over. Furthermore, the Little Entente, historically known as France's satellites, has seen centrifugal forces between Yugoslavia and France increasingly develop in recent years, and the system of the Little Entente is in danger of gradually disintegrating. Since Göring's visit to the Balkans and his friendship with Yugoslavia, this danger is even more likely to become a reality. Currently, only the Soviet Union is on good terms with France, but whether the Soviet Union truly stands on the same front as France remains a significant question. From this, we can say that France has suffered diplomatic failures in recent years. Recently, due to Germany's rearmament, the stalled Eastern European Pact, and the establishment of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement, France's position in Europe has been greatly threatened. After the establishment of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement, the Frenchman Soulzhi wrote an article stating: "Three months ago, Germany reorganized its army and implemented conscription without France's consent, an act that severely struck the dignity of the victorious nations and the treaty. Today, Germany has obtained the consent of Britain, the United States, and Japan to reorganize its navy, making France feel even more deeply wounded! Other countries disregard France's interests; it is now too late for France to force Germany to accept its will!" This is indeed speaking honestly. Thus, France, afflicted by domestic economic panic and financial crisis, and repeatedly failing in diplomacy, inevitably faces an unstable political situation. Judging from the recent situation, it is likely that French politics will take an extreme path, and the life of its democratic politics is in danger of being cut off.

France's situation differs from that of Britain, the United States, and other countries. It does not have large political parties; instead, it is a country where many small parties coexist. In terms of the composition of these small parties and the policies they pursue, they can be divided into three major forces: the left wing, the right wing, and the center wing. In the past, because French society was relatively stable and only needed international coordination externally, the more moderate Radical Socialist Party, representing the liberal citizenry, had repeatedly formed cabinets. However, in recent years, under conditions of economic panic, financial crisis, and diplomatic difficulties, the cabinets of the Radical Socialist Party could not be maintained. First, the Herriot cabinet fell on the issue of war debts, and then the Penggu cabinet resigned due to the budget bill. Following this were the successive collapses of the Daladier, Sarraut, and Chautemps cabinets. After Daladier's second cabinet formation, various right-leaning groups in France held riots in Paris over the Bayonne-Stavisky affair. At the same time, left-wing parties such as the Socialist Party staged a counter-demonstration, turning the normally tranquil France into a turbulent city. The result was the fall of the Daladier cabinet, followed by the formation of the Doumergue cabinet, representing a truce among political parties and national unity. Because Doumergue was a relatively right-leaning figure, the formation of the Doumergue cabinet not only interrupted the Radical Socialist Party's continued cabinet formations but also marked the beginning of the rise of right-leaning politics in France.

Shortly after its formation, the Doumergue cabinet collapsed due to the Radical Socialist Party's opposition to the constitutional reform bill. It was succeeded by the Flandin cabinet. However, the Flandin cabinet was recently overthrown due to the financial plenipotentiary bill. The ensuing Bouisson cabinet lasted only three days, its life cut short by a two-vote difference on the financial plenipotentiary bill. Currently, the Laval cabinet has been formed, and the financial plenipotentiary bill has been passed by both the Senate and the Chamber of Deputies. On the surface, the cabinet turmoil in France has temporarily subsided, but even in the recent past cabinet turmoil, one can see the serious situation of the struggle between the two extreme forces in France.

From the Doumergue cabinet to the Laval cabinet, although there have been some changes in form, in reality, it can be said that it is the development of right-leaning politics in France. It is clear that Doumergue was a figure close to the right wing, Flandin was even the instigator of the Paris events, and Laval was the foreign minister of the Flandin cabinet. According to a Paris newspaper, the Laval government plans to issue substitute legal decrees authorized by the parliament from July 1, with the following content: (1) Reduce or abolish certain types of pensions. (2) Abolish retirement pensions for current military personnel who participated in the war. (3) Abolish secondary railway branch lines and reduce railway personnel. (4) Gradually reduce redundant staff, abolish concurrent positions and certain types of public expenses, and abolish overtime work bonuses. (5) Abolish certain administrative agencies. (6) Revise the social insurance system. If this news is true, then just from this point alone, we can say that the right-leaning performance of the Laval cabinet is even more advanced than that of the Flandin cabinet.

Currently, although the political situation in France is relatively stable on the surface due to the passage of the Laval cabinet's financial plenipotentiary bill, its political crisis is developing day by day. In fact, the "Action Française" organized by the monarchists has recently held demonstrations, destroying the small newspaper advocating for the devaluation of the franc. The "Croix-de-Feu" composed of veterans is now posting slogans all over the country, shouting: "The national treasury is now empty, peace is in jeopardy, the people hope for work and bread, the government that wants to prevent speculation has been overthrown by the parliament within 24 hours, the right-wing members who are slaves to capitalism and the left-wing members who are slaves to Marx are preparing for civil war, we advocate stopping it immediately!" Former Prime Minister Tardieu also opposes the parliamentary system and advocates establishing a strong government to cope with today's "economic difficulties." At the same time, the leaders of the left-wing Socialist Party also explicitly declared that they can cope with all events, and the joint meeting of left-wing parties has also discussed the issue of re-electing the parliament to produce a majority party. Seeing the active activities of the "Croix-de-Feu" and the "National Volunteers," the Radical Socialist Party has decided at its recent caucus meeting to continue holding caucus meetings during the parliamentary recess and to request that the parliamentary committees also continue to meet during the recess. The severity of the situation is evident!

In such a serious situation, we can clearly see that the two extremes of conflict in France are developing. The future of this development will inevitably be the victory of one aspect of the two extremes (left or right), because judging from the current domestic and international situation in France, there is no possibility of victory for moderate sentimentalism. The so-called modern "democracy politics" in France is also in danger of being cut off, and the realization of this danger, judging from the current situation, cannot be said to be in the distant future; perhaps it is happening right now!

Miscellaneous Writings

An Evening Chat on Language Problems 225

— Cao Ju

A: I promised to talk to you about language problems tonight, but because I've been very busy, I haven't prepared well. It would be best if you raise the questions and I answer them.

B: Thank you for making the special trip. Please sit down and talk! The first thing I want to ask is, what is the purpose of Latinizing Chinese?

A: Its purpose is to make the literacy movement easier to succeed so that the illiterate masses who can only speak but not read and write can have a writing system. We know that Chinese pictographs are really too…

B: Too difficult, right?

A: That's right, too difficult. It takes several years to learn a few thousand characters. To be able to freely read and write, it probably takes at least ten years of effort. And most people's lives aren't very good; they really don't have the time or financial means to learn this kind of writing system. That's the first thing.

B: What's the second?

A: The shortcoming of Chinese characters isn't just that they're "difficult," but also that they're "bad." Chinese characters are not suitable for ordinary people's use; they make people "interpret words literally," they can't match spoken language, they're not suitable for children, and they can't accept internationalized roots. That's the second point.

B: Are you saying that we Chinese should abandon thousands of years of Chinese characters and instead learn the foreign devils' gibberish?

A: That's right, Latinization wants to abolish Chinese characters, but the Latinized writing system is still Chinese. The language is Chinese, but it's spelled with Latin letters. So the Latinized Chinese writing system is definitely not the "gibberish" you mentioned. That's the first thing. Second, Latin letters are by no means something that foreigners exclusively own.

B: If they're not the foreign devils', then whose are they?

A: They belong to everyone. Latin letters have gone through many evolutions, and now they have become international things. Not only do I have to use A+B+C... when learning algebra, but also the names of medicines prescribed by doctors, the names of train stations in China and Japan, post office stamps, typewriters, signal flags, ... all need Latin letters. Can you say it's not international? Haha, even the shirt you're wearing is from ABC Company!

B: But I don't understand. Why doesn't Latinization adopt a standard language to unify the whole country, but instead Latinize dialects? Isn't this splitting the Chinese people?

A: First, you need to know that people are not unified by language. The unity and opposition between people are determined by their material interests. Among people with consistent interests, no matter what method you use, you can't prevent their "unity." Conversely, among people with conflicting interests, even if they speak the same language, they have to "oppose" each other. Second, there is currently no nationally unified spoken language in China. You want something that "doesn't exist" to "exist" immediately; not only can Latinization not do it, but neither can any other -ization.

B: Then aren't Chinese characters nationally unified?

A: That's right, Chinese characters are nationally unified. But only two out of ten Chinese people understand Chinese characters. The existence or non-existence of Chinese characters has almost nothing to do with ordinary people. Because of the existence of Chinese characters, they haven't benefited in any way, but have suffered a lot!

B: Then suppose one day, ordinary people's lives get better, and they have time and money. Would it be possible to learn Chinese characters at that time?

A: I don't think so, even if it's as you said, they wouldn't need to do so. Because I've already said that the problem with Chinese characters isn't just that they're "difficult," but also that they're "bad." We already have very good things; why would we want this bad thing again? It's like having steamboats and sailboats; there's no need to sit in a dugout canoe anymore.

B: Then are you saying that you don't want a unified language for the rest of your lives?

A: That's not right. Latinization not only doesn't oppose it but also advocates having a unified language. But the unified language of Latinization is not to force the local dialect of one place on the whole country. Latinization's method is to develop dialects, promote their intermingling, and help the formation of a unified language. Dialects are not the permanent goal of Latinization; we are not "for dialects for the sake of dialects." Dialects are a historical category. With the progress of society and the economy, dialects will inevitably disappear and form a unified language, and finally even a universal language for the whole world. So the Latinization of dialects is a temporary transitional means to achieve a unified national language.

B: Do you mean to let dialects develop naturally and wait for them to form a unified language?

A: Definitely not like that. The formation of a unified language has its objective conditions—changes in the socio-economic structure, the development of transportation, frequent mutual contact and exchange of experiences (oral and written) between people in different places. But there must also be subjective conditions—and that is the progress of culture and education, and in this regard, the vigorous implementation of dialect Latinization and the intermingling of dialects must be the most powerful factors. Objective conditions are certainly fundamental, but if you only rely on the progress of objective conditions without adding subjective promotion and control, the result is often slow, relying on experience without theory, and even taking detours and suffering unnecessary sacrifices.

B: But suppose once Chinese characters are abolished and all places start using Latinization, won't we be returning to an era without writing? For example, if someone from Shanghai goes to Guangdong for investigation or travel, when there are Chinese characters, they can still use the help of Chinese characters to read local newspapers and understand the price lists in hotels and trams, and the menus in restaurants. They can investigate or travel freely. But after the implementation of Latinization, they will find it difficult to move even an inch, as if they have arrived in a foreign country!

A: First, Latinization does not plan to abolish Chinese characters immediately. In the early stages of Latinization, Chinese characters can still exist for a period of time. People who understand Chinese characters will naturally continue to use them, although the scope of use of Chinese characters will gradually narrow and eventually be abandoned. So, to think that after Latinization, we will return to an era without writing is completely an unnecessary worry. Second, I want to ask you what kind of person the Shanghainese you mentioned is. If you're talking about those people whose lives aren't very good, then how can they have the blessing to "investigate" and "travel" to Guangdong? And coolies never look at the menu when they go into small restaurants to eat. So even when there are still Chinese characters, Chinese characters have not given them any convenience, and it is common for them to suffer because of Chinese characters. As for when Latinization becomes widespread, firstly, the transmission and learning of dialects in each region will be extremely easy at that time, and secondly, even if only the writing of the local area is simple, newspapers, price lists, and menus can be printed or written in the writing of each region at that time. Doesn't Shanghai currently have newspapers in five or six languages, and aren't there price lists in English, French, and Chinese on trams, and aren't the menus of Russian restaurants in both Chinese and Russian? Currently, if there is really a Shanghai coolie who can "investigate" in Guangdong, even with Chinese characters, they will find it "difficult to move even an inch, as if they have arrived in a foreign country." But after Latinization is implemented, even without Chinese characters, they can still "investigate or travel freely." If the Shanghainese you're talking about is a comprador in a foreign firm, then it's even less of a problem. Even if they really "arrive in a foreign country," they can bring a translator with them and will definitely not find it "difficult to move even an inch." But Latinization originally had no intention of meddling in whether or not it is convenient for them. In short, judging from your tone, it seems that you are still thinking about the people who already know Chinese characters, and not about the illiterate masses. We must know that since the existence of Chinese characters has nothing to do with ordinary people, they will definitely not suffer because of the abolition of Chinese characters. In the process of Latinization, they have nothing to lose, but something to gain: that is obvious. B judging from your tone, it seems that you advocate immediately using Latinized writing to teach the illiterate, but may I ask, what use is it after learning Latinization? Aren't most of the current newspapers, magazines, and books printed in Chinese characters? A Your question is very reasonable! But I want to ask you in return: how many of the current newspapers printed in Chinese characters are really suitable for the masses to read? What kinds of magazines and books are suitable for them to read? Even if they ate an elixir and could read Chinese characters from tomorrow, they would feel that there is nothing to read. So even if all the illiterate knew Chinese characters, the problem would not be completely solved. Latinization is still in the promotion period, so currently there is nothing for them to read, just like with Chinese characters. But with the spread of Latinization, if those engaged in Latinization can actively compile and print some popular reading materials, after just one year, I'm afraid the masses who already know a little Chinese characters will have nothing to read if they don't pick up Latinization.

B: Then what are your opinions on the "variant characters" advocated by Hu Yuzhi?

A: Although one or two people have supported his advocacy, even he himself has not used "variant characters" to write a second article. From this point, it can be seen how difficult his method is to implement. Moreover, I have always felt that his so-called "variant characters" are not really variant characters, but simplified characters. For example, he uses "贾直" (jia zhi) to replace "价值" (jia zhi, value), instead of using "介之" (jie zhi), which has fewer strokes, is one example. I once carefully did a statistic of the article he published in "Taibai," and the result was that only two or three words were written entirely in variant characters, such as writing "拥护" (yong hu, support) as "永户" (yong hu), and the rest were composed of simplified characters or one variant character and one correct character. Unfortunately, I don't have that piece of paper with me, otherwise I could give you the specific numbers. The most that his method can achieve, that is, the most ideal situation, is the alphabetization of Chinese characters, with each group of homophonic Chinese characters represented by one Chinese character. However, in the Northern dialect, there are about 450 groups of homophonic Chinese characters, which means that his alphabet would have 450 letters, which is more than 420 more than Latinization!

B: Finally, I would also like to hear your opinion on handwritten characters.

A: Handwritten characters mix into the ranks of Chinese characters (correct characters), disrupt the rear of Chinese characters, tear off its dignified coat, and promote its disintegration—in this respect, it can be said to be an ally of Latinization. But its role is limited to this, and it has no active significance beyond that. Moreover, handwritten characters have a very big crisis, which is that as soon as they come out, some people give them too high an evaluation, as if once handwritten characters become popular, the Chinese language problem will be solved. In fact, the change in the shape of the characters, and most of them are just a reduction in strokes, can only provide some writing convenience for people who already know, slightly know, and will know Chinese characters, and there is nothing else. —Oh, it's getting late, see you tomorrow.

B: It's truly "listening to you for one evening is better than reading books for ten years." Let's see each other tomorrow.

Art Scene

Watching the Rehearsal of "Modern Lady" 226

— Yun

When I arrived at the Lakeside Society, it was only half-past eight, but the audience was already full. It took a bit of time to find a seat. I was waiting for the performance of this tragedy with a skeptical gaze. The actors in this play had only trained for three months, but after watching this rehearsal, I really felt a bit surprised! The detailed situation is as follows:

Script: Although it is just a love story, it has considerable value in artistic achievement due to the ingenuity of the composition technique.

Actors: Hong Ying, who plays Shen Xiujuan, performs very fittingly, and her dissolute and bold behavior is very tasteful. Lu Ping, who plays Xiujuan's husband, has natural and calm movements and expressions, but his voice seemed a bit hoarse that day. Dai Hao, who plays Zou Yisheng, has a naturally slippery face and can also perform with great attention to detail. Others, like Yang Duo, Cheng Jingzi, Bai Xiongchang, Fan Yanfu, Huang Yun, Xu Lilin, and Qian Feng, are all extremely competent in the roles they play. In short, in the entire performance, in the performance of each actor, I can say that there is considerable success.

Lighting: It is said that it was temporarily rented, but the results were not bad.

Set design: There is also nothing to criticize, except that the movements were a bit too slow when the two acts were replaced, which slightly made people feel unpleasant.

Other: In terms of dubbing, it is also very consistent with the plot. However, if the tragic scene in the fifth act could be aided by the power of music to increase the audience's sympathy, it would probably make the plot more vivid!

After Watching "The Beginning of Man" 227

— Qin

The Yihua sound film "The Beginning of Man," which recently premiered at the Jincheng Grand Theater, can be said to be a good film worth watching in all aspects. What particularly interested me was that this film also touched on the issue of language and writing.

Boatman Zhang Ronggen and his wife, due to the difficulty of making a living, sent their newly born child, Ren Di, to the wealthy gentleman Huang Zijing to be his son. The grief of Ronggen and his wife in sending away "their own flesh" to someone else is needless to say. After taking the child to Huang's house, Mr. Huang came out with a written contract and asked, "Ronggen, can you read?"

"I know a few words, sir, please read it once!" Tears were shining.

In Mr. Huang's solemn reading, Ronggen and his wife were trembling and sobbing. They didn't understand what was written on it. They didn't need to understand; in the end, they affixed their seals. The rough hands accustomed to holding oars tightly grasped a thin pen, the hand trembling, holding back tears, and drew a cross in the low weeping of his wife.

Ronggen's wife had worked in Mr. Huang's factory for more than ten years and had become a cripple, sick in bed all day, calling out the name of Ren Di, who had already become the young master. Ronggen, in order to comfort his dying wife, planned to go to the accounting room to steal a photo of the young master Ren Di, but was caught and taken to court as a petty thief. Ronggen said that the young master was his own son. The judge asked:

"What evidence do you have?"

"There is a piece of paper," Ronggen replied.

"What does it say?" the judge asked.

"..." Ronggen couldn't answer; he couldn't even find the piece of paper. So he was put on trial as a petty thief.

This is precisely the greatest effect of the current Chinese characters, a concrete example of how pictographic Chinese characters serve people like Mr. Huang.

In addition, the Suzhou dialect folk song that Xiaogen and Jindi sang during their love affair, and the Suzhou dialect storytelling broadcast on the radio, also show that the director used dialects very appropriately. The scene of Ronggen reading the comic strip "Xue Rengui Conquers the East" under the lamp also greatly interested me.

Small Monograph

The Revival of the Queen of Science (Part 1) 229

— Chen

Those who study philosophy often fear being asked, "What is philosophy?" but they fear even more being asked, "What is the use of philosophy?" This is a question in the history of philosophy. From the great Greek philosopher Socrates onwards, all the way to the medieval scholastic school, which specialized in playing tricks with syllogisms without studying practical issues externally, philosophy was a living science. It studied everything in the universe, was respected by people, regarded as a guide for personal conduct, and revered as the queen of science. But after the Middle Ages, philosophy became dead. Descartes said, "I think, therefore I am." He placed everything in the universe in thought and then passed thought through the immaterial soul, "I." Could this solve the problems of life? Since philosophy began engaging in debates within the ivory tower of epistemology, not only has its territory been almost entirely occupied by science, but it has also been met with cold looks and forgotten by people. You see, in modern philosophy, it no longer studies practical life issues, but has become dry questions of mind and matter, questions of substance and phenomena, questions of reason and sensation.

The above continues from page five.

Page 22

Page 23

Forgetting the search for truth and wisdom, forgetting the influence on the meaning of life, philosophy is on the road to ruin.

Now, let's take another look at real life! Since the flourishing of science and the Industrial Revolution in the nineteenth century, people have lived in a trivial, disturbing, and mechanical world. The natural principles of morality and religious belief have been destroyed. Luxurious and sensual life has replaced asceticism, and restless stimulation has replaced contentment. Chemical warfare is lurking everywhere. All new perspectives on sexual relationships and even illusions of the soul are wriggling on the earth. Except for mechanism and fatalism, people can no longer find a destination for life. As for philosophy itself, the former cosmology has become astronomy and geophysics, the former "natural science" has become biology and physics, and the current "spiritual philosophy" will become psychology. "Philosophy is finished!" Everyone may shout in unison!

But, is philosophy really finished? No! You see, what mathematicians indicate are just abstract theories and dry programs. What biologists are debating are the issues of "gradual change," "mutation," "innate," and "acquired." Although psychologists emphasize the analysis of behavior, they are also just terms such as "brain," "glands," "senses," "muscles," "response," and "stimulus," etc., which are difficult to contribute to practical life issues. This task can only be undertaken by philosophy. Philosophy will delineate the entire perspective, encompass all of life, and seek a consistent spiritual endeavor from a chaotic state, including various issues that can affect the value and meaning of life. Philosophy must, like science, use some method to "compensate" for the "deficiencies" of life, just as medicine compensates for diseases, and these deficiencies arise from desires.

There is a slogan now, which is that there is only a philosophy of life, not philosophy. In fact, it only observed a part and did not deeply investigate the whole. We know that everything in the universe only has value when it is related to human desires—just like studying economics—; but desires are changeable and impermanent, and only philosophy can make them consistent or coordinated; this is difficult to achieve with knowledge and tools (science). This is the issue of science and philosophy. For example, a scientist, regarding chlorine, only says what the compounds or components of chlorine are and what its effects are. However, the study of the ultimate issues in life, such as whether human culture, virtues, knowledge, works of art, and all constructions should be destroyed, is the task of philosophy. Also, for example, a black woman with dark skin and lips is clearly considered extremely beautiful by a great man of the same race. Is a life immersed in wealth sweet? Or is a life bathed in creation sweet? These many questions cannot be illuminated by science. This is the difference between science and philosophy. Then can philosophy become a scholastic school without science? This is also wrong. Because if human wisdom does not have science as a foundation, it cannot grow to maturity, and may even become corrupt and dishonest, and become alienated from human life. At the same time, if science has no philosophical meaning, it becomes cruel and meaningless. They are mutually dependent. To sum up the above, the tasks of philosophy are roughly these: (1) To study the ultimate and final questions with a comprehensive perspective; (2) To use various sciences as the foundation of the entirety of the universe, reside above science, and use a condescending "attitude" to solve problems that science cannot solve (such as the universe and life); (3) To peel away phenomena and study the noumenon (science studies phenomena, such as natural phenomena and social phenomena, while philosophy studies the noumenon, such as mind and matter). (To be continued)

Movie News

Moonlight News Bulletin 233

Moonlight's first all-singing, all-talking giant film "Sound Madness" will be released simultaneously in four ports. As the release date approaches, the four new copies are being rushed out. Due to time constraints, the coloring work in the film cannot be as extensive as expected. However, everything in "Sound Madness" will surely satisfy the audience.

The Moonlight Special Issue was originally scheduled to be released with "Sound Madness," but due to the busy schedules of various departments, the photography and plate-making cannot be completed on time, so it will be delayed by one or two periods before meeting readers.

With the release of "Sound Madness," the "Sound Madness" song will be broadcast on the air. The record is No. 34919, issued by the Baidai Company, and is available in various record stores.

Paris Premieres Spring Light of Formosa 234

The film "Spring Light of Formosa" is a great production of Paramount Company in 1935, costing more than 800,000 gold to complete. The entire film is colorful and dazzling. The plot tells that the people of Bali Island in India are bound by religion. If a young girl is rejected by a man's love, she is considered a great shame and must be cremated. The film was a sensation at its premiere at the Da Guangming. This time, it's making a comeback and is said to be playing at the Paris Theater starting yesterday. The audience is very crowded, so those who want to see the film should not miss it.

Drama News Bulletin 235

First-Class Staff

Not only are the actors in this "Nora" performance all stars and veterans from the film and theater circles, but the stage staff are also all first-class figures in the Shanghai stage. For example, Fan Bozi and Ouyang Shanzun's lighting, Song Xiaojiang's makeup, Zheng Shanzun's props, Zhu Jinming's installations, Yang Qiming's photography, and Wang Qi's costumes are all members of various large and small performances, which can be said to be a collection of the most outstanding staff in the film and theater circles.

Stage Installation Releases a Special Radiance

Chinese stage installations have generally been taken from Japan or the United States. Recently, American-style scenery has become more popular on Chinese stages. Watching this kind of scenery that often does not change will show the superficiality and low-level taste of the performance. This "Nora" performance, like the Reinhardt Theater, collects multifaceted stage designs to complete a realistic 19th-century set. The carvings on the walls and the window decorations have all been carefully studied, which can be said to break the current record of stage design.

The Trilogy of Lights

The lighting of the Nora performance is the responsibility of Ouyang Shanzun and Fan Bozi. The three acts are divided into morning, dusk, and snowy night. Now, the effect of the lights distinguishes these three time periods.

Serenade in Nostalgia 236

Dusk has arrived;

Little stars shine high,

The light is faint,

The sound is quiet,

As if guarding people to sleep.

Children rest,

Mothers smile;

There are trees by the pond,

Many birds perch,

Dense leaves face the wind,

Low branches cover the dew,

As if people are resting at home,

The door will not open until tomorrow.

New Publication Introduction 237

The maiden issue of the "Movie News" pictorial weekly is scheduled to be released on July 6th. The content is very good, and there is a "Service" column, which employs many film veterans to answer readers' questions about various departments of film art. The answers will be published in the magazine on a regular basis. Inquiries are welcome. The address of the society is Room 6, 3rd Floor, No. 390 Nanjing Road.
